Vail found himself painting brain-pictures of the future of the telephone, and by the time that he was asked to become its General Manager, he had become so confident that, as he said afterwards, he "was willing to leave a Government job with a small salary for a telephone job with no salary."

    正如阿莫斯·肯德尔三十年前离开邮政系统创办电报公司一样，西奥多·N·韦尔也离开了邮政系统创办了电话公司。他曾管理过三千五百名邮政员工，并开发了一套覆盖全国所有有人居住地区的系统。因此，他拥有丰富的经验，这对于理顺错综复杂的电话业务至关重要。他逐条制定了方法、政策和系统。他为电话业务引入了更宏观的视角，并彻底否决了所有出售公司的计划。他成功说服了六位邮政界的朋友购买股票，因此，不到两个月，第一家“贝尔电话公司”就成立了，拥有45万美元的资本和一万两千部电话的服务。

    So, just as Amos Kendall had left the post office service thirty years before to establish the telegraph business, Theodore N. Vail left the post office service to establish the telephone business. He had been in authority over thirty-five hundred postal employees, and was the developer of a system that covered every inhabited portion of the country. Consequently, he had a quality of experience that was immensely valuable in straightening out the tangled affairs of the telephone. Line by line, he mapped out a method, a policy, a system. He introduced a larger view of the telephone business, and swept off the table all schemes for selling out. He persuaded half a dozen of his post office friends to buy stock, so that in less than two months the first "Bell Telephone Company" was organized, with $450,000 capital and a service of twelve thousand telephones.

    韦尔的第一步自然是巩固这家小公司的根基，防止西联公司吓得它投降。他立即将贝尔的专利副本寄给每一位代理商，命令他们坚守阵地，抵御一切反对。“我们拥有唯一的原创电话专利，”他写道，“我们一手创建并开创了这项业务，我们绝不允许任何公司将其夺走。”他对一位亮出白羽毛的代理商写道：

    Vail's first step, naturally, was to stiffen up the backbone of this little company, and to prevent the Western Union from frightening it into a surrender. He immediately sent a copy of Bell's patent to every agent, with orders to hold the fort against all opposition. "We have the only original telephone patents," he wrote; "we have organized and introduced the business, and we do not propose to have it taken from us by any corporation." To one agent, who was showing the white feather, he wrote:

    “你对西联公司的期望太高了。如果它全部集中在你所在的城市，你或许会感到害怕；但它在那里只有一个代表，而且除了电话业务之外，他大概也忙不过来了。你承认自己无法与他的影响力抗衡，而你又把这作为你的专长，这实在说不过去。或许会有十几家公司都转投西联公司，但他们不可能把所有的朋友都带走。我建议你继续保持目前的优势。我们必须组建足够强大的公司来与之抗争，因为如果成立的公司遇到一点阻力就倒下，那根本毫无意义。”

    "You have too great an idea of the Western Union. If it was all massed in your one city you might well fear it; but it is represented there by one man only, and he has probably as much as he can attend to outside of the telephone. For you to acknowledge that you cannot compete with his influence when you make it your special business, is hardly the thing. There may be a dozen concerns that will all go to the Western Union, but they will not take with them all their friends. I would advise that you go ahead and keep your present advantage. We must organize companies with sufficient vitality to carry on a fight, as it is simply useless to get a company started that will succumb to the first bit of opposition it may encounter."

    接下来，在安抚了那些惊恐万分的代理商之后，韦尔着手制定一套明确的商业策略。他加强了合同的力度，并将合同期限缩短至五年。他限制每位代理商只能在一个地方开展业务，并保留了连接不同城市的所有权利。他设立了一个部门，专门负责收集和保护所有与电话相关的新发明。他同意，如果任何本地公司选择以股票形式偿还债务，他将以股票的形式收取部分专利费。此外，他还采取措施，通过控制电话设备的生产工厂，来实现所有电话设备的标准化。

    Next, having encouraged his thoroughly alarmed agents, Vail proceeded to build up a definite business policy. He stiffened up the contracts and made them good for five years only. He confined each agent to one place, and reserved all rights to connect one city with another. He established a department to collect and pro- tect any new inventions that concerned the telephone. He agreed to take part of the royalties in stock, when any local company preferred to pay its debts in this way. And he took steps toward standardizing all telephonic apparatus by controlling the factories that made it.

    这些措施都是韦尔创建全国电话系统计划的一部分。从一开始，他的核心理念就不是简单地租赁电话，而是创建一个联邦公司，作为整个电话业务的永久合作伙伴。即使在那个一切都还很琐碎的年代，在开拓的混乱和磕磕绊绊中，他也制定了如今仍然适用的总体政策；这在很大程度上解释了为什么美国的电话数量是其他所有国家电话数量总和的两倍。

    These various measures were part of Vail's plan to create a national telephone system. His central idea, from the first, was not the mere leasing of telephones, but rather the creation of a Federal company that would be a permanent partner in the entire telephone business. Even in that day of small things, and amidst the confusion and rough-and-tumble of pioneering, he worked out the broad policy that prevails to-day; and this goes far to explain the fact that there are in the United States twice as many telephones as there are in all other countries combined.

    韦尔的到来就像布吕歇尔在滑铁卢战役中一样——稍稍迟到，但及时阻止了电话部队被西部联合公司的老牌势力击溃。他刚坐上经理的宝座，西部联合公司就推出了爱迪生发射机，让整个贝尔公司陷入混乱。当时，爱迪生刚刚开始他的发明生涯，他制造的发射机灵敏度极高。毫无疑问，它比当时使用的电话机要好得多，贝尔电话公司的租户们异口同声地要求“配备一台像爱迪生发射机一样好的发射机”。当然，这不可能一蹴而就，接下来的五个月是电话发展史上最黑暗的时期。

    Vail arrived very much as Blucher did at the battle of Waterloo--a trifle late, but in time to prevent the telephone forces from being routed by the Old Guard of the Western Union. He was scarcely seated in his managerial chair, when the Western Union threw the entire Bell army into confusion by launching the Edison transmitter. Edison, who was at that time fairly started in his career of wizardry, had made an instrument of marvellous alertness. It was beyond all argument superior to the telephones then in use and the lessees of Bell telephones clamored with one voice for "a transmitter as good as Edison's." This, of course, could not be had in a moment, and the five months that followed were the darkest days in the childhood of the telephone.

    如何与拥有先进发射机、众多代理商、庞大电报网络、四千万美元资本，以及对所有报纸、酒店、铁路和通行权拥有优先权的西联公司竞争——这是新任总经理面临的首要问题。每一步进步都得靠自己争取。他的几位主管离职，他被迫接管那些亏损的分公司。几乎每一封邮件都给他带来沮丧或失败的消息。

    How to compete with the Western Union, which had this superior transmitter, a host of agents, a network of wires, forty millions of capital, and a first claim upon all newspapers, hotels, railroads, and rights of way--that was the immediate problem that confronted the new General Manager. Every inch of progress had to be fought for. Several of his captains deserted, and he was compelled to take control of their unprofitable exchanges. There was scarcely a mail that did not bring him some bulletin of discouragement or defeat.

    为了安抚敌对的公众，各地的电话资费都定得太低了。哈伯德曾将私人线路两部电话的年费定为二十美元；而当交换机开始运营时，月费也很少超过三美元。大量电话无人接听，其中大部分是官员和政客。在圣路易斯——少数几个收费合理的城市之一——十分之九的商家拒绝成为订户。在波士顿，第一个付费电话站运营了三个月才赚到一美元。即使到了1880年，在尼亚加拉大瀑布召开的第一届全国电话大会上，一位代表对当时的普遍情况的描述也十分准确：“我们都处于一种充满热情却又忐忑不安的状态。我们满怀希望，但仔细分析这些希望，却发现它们实在太不切实际了。可能没有一家公司能说自己赚了一分钱，甚至连预期能赚一分钱都不敢说。”

    In the effort to conciliate a hostile public, the telephone rates had everywhere been made too low. Hubbard had set a price of twenty dollars a year, for the use of two telephones on a private line; and when exchanges were started, the rate was seldom more than three dollars a month. There were deadheads in abundance, mostly officials and politicians. In St. Louis, one of the few cities that charged a sufficient price, nine- tenths of the merchants refused to become subscribers. In Boston, the first pay-station ran three months before it earned a dollar. Even as late as 1880, when the first National Telephone Convention was held at Niagara Falls, one of the delegates expressed the general situation very correctly when he said: "We were all in a state of enthusiastic uncertainty. We were full of hope, yet when we analyzed those hopes they were very airy indeed. There was probably not one company that could say it was making a cent, nor even that it EXPECTED to make a cent."

    尤其是在西部联合公司势力最强大的大城市，电话先驱们的生活充满了艰辛和冒险。例如，在费城，一位名叫托马斯·E·康尼什的意志坚定的年轻人，在着手建立第一条电话服务时，却遭到了如同公敌般的攻击。没有一位官员愿意给他颁发架设电线的许可证。他的工人被逮捕。印刷电报公司的人警告他，要么放弃，要么被赶走。当他向资本家寻求资金时，他们却回答说，他不如去租口簧琴，而不是电话。最终，在辩论失败后，他不得不诉诸策略。他接到了托马斯·斯科特上校的命令，斯科特上校希望在他的住所和办公室之间架设一条电线。斯科特上校是宾夕法尼亚铁路公司的总裁，因此在费城享有极高的声望。所以，康尼什一架设好这条线路，就让他的工人继续架设其他线路。警察介入时，他出示了斯科特上校的签名，警察便放他走了。就这样，他在骗局被识破之前架设了十五条电线；不久之后，他带着八位订户，创办了费城第一家电信交易所。

    Especially in the largest cities, where the Western Union had most power, the lives of the telephone pioneers were packed with hardships and adventures. In Philadelphia, for instance, a resolute young man named Thomas E. Cornish was attacked as though he had suddenly become a public enemy, when he set out to establish the first telephone service. No official would grant him a permit to string wires. His workmen were arrested. The printing-telegraph men warned him that he must either quit or be driven out. When he asked capitalists for money, they replied that he might as well expect to lease jew's- harps as telephones. Finally, he was compelled to resort to strategy where argument had failed. He had received an order from Colonel Thomas Scott, who wanted a wire between his house and his office. Colonel Scott was the President of the Pennsylvania Railroad, and therefore a man of the highest prestige in the city. So as soon as Cornish had put this line in place, he kept his men at work stringing other lines. When the police interfered, he showed them Colonel Scott's signature and was let alone. In this way he put fifteen wires up before the trick was discovered; and soon afterwards, with eight subscribers, he founded the first Philadelphia exchange.

    可以想象，这样的争斗并没有给母公司带来多少收入；桑德斯当时写的信件证明，母公司当时处境艰难。

    As may be imagined, such battling as this did not put much money into the treasury of the parent company; and the letters written by Sanders at this time prove that it was in a hard plight.

    以下是桑德斯不堪重负地向哈伯德提出的问题之一：

    The following was one of the queries put to Hubbard by the overburdened Sanders:

    “你究竟指望我如何在国库空空如也、债务高达三万美元的情况下，支付两百七十五美元的汇票？”他在第二封信中继续写道，“韦尔的薪水本来就少，但他的钱从哪里来，我就不清楚了。布拉德利垂头丧气，意志消沉。威廉姆斯一直催我钱，我的个人信用也经不起这样的折腾。今天我已经预支了公司两千美元，威廉姆斯这个月还得再借三千美元。他的发薪日到了，但他的资金已经捉襟见肘。如果布拉德利束手无策，我就把我最后的孤注一掷的计划告诉你。”

    "How on earth do you expect me to meet a draft of two hundred and seventy-five dollars without a dollar in the treasury, and with a debt of thirty thousand dollars staring us in the face?" "Vail's salary is small enough," he continued in a second letter, "but as to where it is coming from I am not so clear. Bradley is awfully blue and discouraged. Williams is tormenting me for money and my personal credit will not stand everything. I have advanced the Company two thousand dollars to-day, and Williams must have three thousand dollars more this month. His pay-day has come and his capital will not carry him another inch. If Bradley throws up his hand, I will unfold to you my last desperate plan."

    如果公司资金匮乏，信用也就更差。有一次，韦尔向纽约戴伊街15号一位名叫蒂洛森的商人订购了一批小额货物，商人回复说货物已经备齐，账单也已准备好，账单金额为七美元。巧合的是，如今纽约电话公司那座宏伟的大楼就矗立在蒂洛森商店的原址上。

    And if the company had little money, it had less credit. Once when Vail had ordered a small bill of goods from a merchant named Tillotson, of 15 Dey Street, New York, the merchant replied that the goods were ready, and so was the bill, which was seven dollars. By a strange coincidence, the magnificent building of the New York Telephone Company stands to-day on the site of Tillotson's store.

    贝尔公司这家小公司月复一月地勉强维持生计。员工的工资从未全额发放，有时甚至连续几周都拿不到工资。沃森的笔记本里记录着这段时期的种种琐事，比如“借给贝尔五毛钱”、“借给哈伯德二十毛钱”、“买了一瓶啤酒——可惜不能天天喝啤酒”。如果不是公司唯一的职员德文郡把餐盒里的食物分给他，哈伯德不止一次挨饿。这个小团队里的每个人都饱受嘲讽和诱惑的困扰。有人出价一万美元想买下沃森十分之一的股份，沃森犹豫了三天后才拒绝。铁路公司给韦尔开出了更高更稳定的薪水，条件是让他负责他们的邮件业务。至于桑德斯，他的荒唐行径成了哈弗希尔镇的热门话题。哈弗希尔的一位资本家EJM·黑尔在街上拦住他问道：“桑德斯先生，您不是有个不错的皮革生意吗？”“是的，”桑德斯回答。“那，”黑尔说，“你最好专心经营，别再吹奏管乐器了。”桑德斯的银行家也有一次感到不安，要求他去银行一趟。“桑德斯先生，”银行家说，“如果您能把那些电话股票从银行取出来，换上您那张三万美元的票据，我将不胜感激。我预计几天后审查员会来，我可不想因为银行里有这些东西而被查出来。”

    Month after month, the little Bell Company lived from hand to mouth. No salaries were paid in full. Often, for weeks, they were not paid at all. In Watson's note-book there are such entries during this period as "Lent Bell fifty cents," "Lent Hubbard twenty cents," "Bought one bottle beer--too bad can't have beer every day." More than once Hubbard would have gone hungry had not Devonshire, the only clerk, shared with him the contents of a dinner-pail. Each one of the little group was beset by taunts and temptations. Watson was offered ten thousand dollars for his one-tenth interest, and hesitated three days before refusing it. Railroad companies offered Vail a salary that was higher and sure, if he would superintend their mail business. And as for Sanders, his folly was the talk of Haverhill. One Haverhill capitalist, E. J. M. Hale, stopped him on the street and asked, "Have n't you got a good leather business, Mr. Sanders?" "Yes," replied Sanders. "Well," said Hale, "you had better attend to it and quit playing on wind instruments." Sanders's banker, too, became uneasy on one occasion and requested him to call at the bank. "Mr. Sanders," he said, "I will be obliged if you will take that telephone stock out of the bank, and give me in its place your note for thirty thousand dollars. I am expecting the examiner here in a few days, and I don't want to get caught with that stuff in the bank."

    就在这场经济萧条的午夜时分，可怜的贝尔从英国——他和新婚妻子在那里度蜜月的地方——回来，宣布自己身无分文；他在英国建立电话业务的计划失败了；他急需一千美元来偿还债务。他彻底灰心丧气，病倒了。躺在麻省总医院里，他给那家正拼死捍卫他专利的小公司写了一封求助信。“现在全国各地都有成千上万部电话在运行，”他说，“但我的发明却一分钱也没给我带来。相反，我的研究让我损失惨重，仅仅我三年来为之牺牲的职业价值就高达一万两千美元。”

    Then, in the very midnight of this depression, poor Bell returned from England, whither he and his bride had gone on their honeymoon, and announced that he had no money; that he had failed to establish a telephone business in England; and that he must have a thousand dollars at once to pay his urgent debts. He was thoroughly discouraged and sick. As he lay in the Massachusetts General Hospital, he wrote a cry for help to the embattled little company that was making its desperate fight to protect his patents. "Thousands of telephones are now in operation in all parts of the country," he said, "yet I have not yet received one cent from my invention. On the contrary, I am largely out of pocket by my researches, as the mere value of the profession that I have sacrificed during my three years' work, amounts to twelve thousand dollars."

    幸运的是，几乎与贝尔的信同时寄来的还有一位名叫弗朗西斯·布莱克的波士顿年轻人的来信，信中带来了好消息：他发明了一种与爱迪生的发射机一样令人满意的发射机，并且他更愿意用股票而不是现金来出售。如果说世上真有救星，那非弗朗西斯·布莱克莫属。他的发射机的问世，立刻让贝尔公司在设备方面与西部联合公司并驾齐驱。这鼓舞了少数已经投资的资本家，也激励了其他人加入投资行列。此时，整体商业环境已趋于稳定，四个月后，公司投入使用的电话数量达到了2.2万部，并重组为国家贝尔电话公司，拥有85万美元的资本，由福布斯上校担任首任总裁。福布斯接过了桑德斯长期以来承担的重任。作为一位东印度商人的儿子和拉尔夫·沃尔多·爱默生的女婿，他是一位出身婆罗门阶层的波士顿人。他身材魁梧，四肢方正，既受人爱戴又办事高效；他在这次危机中的领导作用具有巨大的价值。

    Fortunately, there came, in almost the same mail with Bell's letter, another letter from a young Bostonian named Francis Blake, with the good news that he had invented a transmitter as satisfactory as Edison's, and that he would prefer to sell it for stock instead of cash. If ever a man came as an angel of light, that man was Francis Blake. The possession of his transmitter instantly put the Bell Company on an even footing with the Western Union, in the matter of apparatus. It encouraged the few capitalists who had invested money, and it stirred others to come forward. The general business situation had by this time become more settled, and in four months the company had twenty-two thousand telephones in use, and had reorganized into the National Bell Telephone Company, with $850, 000 capital and with Colonel Forbes as its first President. Forbes now picked up the load that had been carried so long by Sanders. As the son of an East India merchant and the son-in-law of Ralph Waldo Emerson, he was a Bostonian of the Brahmin caste. He was a big, four- square man who was both popular and efficient; and his leadership at this crisis was of immense value.

    这次重组将电话业务的各个环节都交到了精明能干的商人手中，也结束了那段充满英雄气概和实验性质的时期。从此以后，电话在金融界有了强大的支持者。它遭到了西联公司的攻击，也遭到了嫉妒贝尔成就的竞争对手的攻击。低廉的资费让它捉襟见肘，笨拙的设备也让它举步维艰。它还饱受着急躁的公众的谩骂和抱怨。但电话的制造和销售技术最终发展成为一项商业活动。如今，它已成为一家为生存而战的企业。

    This reorganization put the telephone business into the hands of competent business men at every point. It brought the heroic and experimental period to an end. From this time onwards the telephone had strong friends in the financial world. It was being attacked by the Western Union and by rival inventors who were jealous of Bell's achievement. It was being half-starved by cheap rates and crippled by clumsy apparatus. It was being abused and grumbled at by an impatient public. But the art of making and marketing it had at last been built up into a commercial enterprise. It was now a business, fighting for its life.

    第三章 企业持有

    CHAPTER III. THE HOLDING OF THE BUSINESS

    在长达十七个月的时间里，没有人质疑贝尔自称是电话的原创发明者。所有的荣誉，即便只是荣誉，也都是无偿授予他的，没有人站出来说这并非他应得的。据我们所知，也没有人强烈希望这样做。没有人想到电话会成为科学界的一件奇特发明。它如此新颖，如此出乎意料，以至于从开尔文勋爵到电报局的信使，所有人都感到难以置信。但是，在贝尔面向两万多人进行公开演讲，阐述了他的发明之后；在费城百年庆典上展出数月之后；在报纸和科学杂志上发表了数百篇关于电话的文章之后；在全国各地实际销售电话之后，开始出现一系列声称拥有电话发明权和侵权的人，以至于健忘的公众开始相信，电话和大多数发明一样，是许多人共同努力的成果。

    For seventeen months no one disputed Bell's claim to be the original inventor of the telephone. All the honor, such as it was, had been given to him freely, and no one came forward to say that it was not rightfully his. No one, so far as we know, had any strong desire to do so. No one conceived that the telephone would ever be any more than a whimsical oddity of science. It was so new, so unexpected, that from Lord Kelvin down to the messenger boys in the telegraph offices, it was an incomprehensible surprise. But after Bell had explained his invention in public lectures before more than twenty thousand people, after it had been on exhibition for months at the Philadelphia Centennial, after several hundred articles on it had appeared in newspapers and scientific magazines, and after actual sales of telephones had been made in various parts of the country, there began to appear such a succession of claimants and infringers that the forgetful public came to believe that the telephone, like most inventions, was the product of many minds.

    正如1837年美国电报的唯一发明者莫尔斯在1838年面临62位竞争对手一样，1876年电话的唯一发明者贝尔两年后也几乎被电话的“蒂奇伯恩发明者”们团团围住。那些曾与他竞争音乐电报的发明家们，如今却自认为无意中做出了与他一样多的贡献。任何拥有电报专利、使用过“会说话的电线”这一常用短语的人，都有机会编造出一个看似合理的“先于发明”的故事。而其他人提出的主张则含糊不清、难以捉摸，以至于如果歌德的继承人以浮士德曾说过“在流动的空气中架起一座桥梁”为由，要求分享电话专利费，贝尔恐怕也不会感到更加惊讶。

    Just as Morse, who was the sole inventor of the American telegraph in 1837, was confronted by sixty-two rivals in 1838, so Bell, who was the sole inventor in 1876, found himself two years later almost mobbed by the "Tichborne claimants" of the telephone. The inventors who had been his competitors in the attempt to produce a musical telegraph, persuaded themselves that they had unconsciously done as much as he. Any possessor of a telegraphic patent, who had used the common phrase "talking wire," had a chance to build up a plausible story of prior invention. And others came forward with claims so vague and elusive that Bell would scarcely have been more surprised if the heirs of Goethe had demanded a share of the telephone royalties on the ground that Faust had spoken of "making a bridge through the moving air."

    这群发明家和冒名顶替者让贝尔大吃一惊，也让他的支持者们感到不安。但这其实也在意料之中。贝尔获得了一项专利——“有史以来最有价值的单一专利”——然而这项发明本身却如此简单，任何一个聪明的孩子或任何一个普通的机械师都能轻易复制。制造电话就像哥伦布把鸡蛋竖起来一样容易。对于那些懂得方法的人来说，没有什么比这更容易的了。于是，当贝尔最初的电话模型简陋地躺在专利局里，除了几句精明的律师可能会钻空子的措辞之外，没有任何保护措施时，一场耗资巨大、旷日持久的专利战就此爆发，这场战争持续了十一年，涉及六百起诉讼，是任何国家历史上耗资最大的专利战。

    This babel of inventors and pretenders amazed Bell and disconcerted his backers. But it was no more than might have been expected. Here was a patent--"the most valuable single patent ever issued"--and yet the invention itself was so simple that it could be duplicated easily by any smart boy or any ordinary mechanic. The making of a telephone was like the trick of Columbus standing an egg on end. Nothing was easier to those who knew how. And so it happened that, as the crude little model of Bell's original telephone lay in the Patent Office open and unprotected except by a few phrases that clever lawyers might evade, there sprang up inevitably around it the most costly and persistent Patent War that any country has ever known, continuing for eleven years and comprising SIX HUNDRED LAWSUITS.

    对新兴的电话行业发起首次攻击的是西部联合电报公司。它全力以赴地向贝尔发起挑战，将爱迪生、格雷和多尔贝尔这三位发明家推向了风口浪尖。它原本以为会轻松取胜；事实上，双方实力差距如此悬殊，似乎根本没有任何胜算。“西部联合电报公司将会吞并电话行业，”公众舆论如此说道，“就像它已经吞并了电报领域的所有进步一样。”

    The first attack upon the young telephone business was made by the Western Union Telegraph Company. It came charging full tilt upon Bell, driving three inventors abreast--Edison, Gray, and Dolbear. It expected an easy victory; in fact, the disparity between the two opponents was so evident, that there seemed little chance of a contest of any kind. "The Western Union will swallow up the telephone people," said public opinion, "just as it has already swallowed up all improvements in telegraphy."

    当时，西联公司是唯一一家业务遍及全国的公司。它是当时世界上最强大的电力公司，正如贝尔写给父母的信中所说，“或许是史上最大的公司”。它不仅拥有四千万美元的资本，还拥有范德比尔特家族的声望，以及各地金融家的青睐。此外，它与电话先驱们处处碰面，因为它本身也是一家电线公司。它拥有沿路和屋顶的通行权，垄断了酒店和铁路办公室。无论贝尔公司朝哪个方向发展，西联公司的电线都横亘在它面前。

    At that time, it should be remembered, the Western Union was the only corporation that was national in its extent. It was the most powerful electrical company in the world, and, as Bell wrote to his parents, "probably the largest corporation that ever existed." It had behind it not only forty millions of capital, but the prestige of the Vanderbilts, and the favor of financiers everywhere. Also, it met the telephone pioneers at every point because it, too, was a WIRE company. It owned rights-of-way along roads and on house-tops. It had a monopoly of hotels and railroad offices. No matter in what direction the Bell Company turned, the live wire of the Western Union lay across its path.

    从一开始，西联公司就更依赖自身实力而非论据。其首席电气专家弗兰克·L·波普花了六个月时间研究贝尔的专利。他买下了美国和欧洲所有可能涉及语音传输的书籍，并聘请了一位精通八种语言的教授进行翻译。他和他的团队搜遍了图书馆和专利局；他们四处搜寻、调查、采访；却一无所获。在提交给西联公司的最终报告中，波普先生宣称，除了贝尔的方法之外，别无他法制造电话，并建议购买贝尔的专利。“我完全找不到任何能够预示贝尔发明的装置或方法，”他说，“因此，我认为他的专利有效。”然而，这家大公司的官员们却拒绝认真对待这份报告。他们将其弃之不顾，转而聘请爱迪生、格雷和多尔贝尔设计一种能够与贝尔的电话竞争的产品。

    From the first, the Western Union relied more upon its strength than upon the merits of its case. Its chief electrical expert, Frank L. Pope, had made a six months' examination of the Bell patents. He had bought every book in the United States and Europe that was likely to have any reference to the transmission of speech, and employed a professor who knew eight languages to translate them. He and his men ransacked libraries and patent offices; they rummaged and sleuthed and interviewed; and found nothing of any value. In his final report to the Western Union, Mr. Pope announced that there was no way to make a telephone except Bell's way, and advised the purchase of the Bell patents. "I am entirely unable to discover any apparatus or method anticipating the invention of Bell as a whole," he said; "and I conclude that his patent is valid." But the officials of the great corporation refused to take this report seriously. They threw it aside and employed Edison, Gray, and Dolbear to devise a telephone that could be put into competition with Bell's.

    正如我们在前一章中看到的，接下来是一段激烈的竞争时期，这段时期后来被称为电话行业的黑暗时代。西联公司收购了贝尔公司的几家交换机，并向其他交换机发起了猛烈的攻势。西联公司凭借其庞大的规模，声称拥有所有股份。它将格雷标榜为电话的发明者，并指示其律师立即对贝尔公司提起诉讼，指控其侵犯了格雷的专利。西联公司希望这种强硬的手段能够迅速迫使规模较小的贝尔公司屈服。每天早上，西联公司都盼望着贝尔公司总部升起白旗。然而，白旗并未出现。相反，贝尔公司却传来消息，他们已经聘请了两位杰出的律师，准备迎战。

    As we have seen in the previous chapter, there now came a period of violent competition which is remembered as the Dark Ages of the telephone business. The Western Union bought out several of the Bell exchanges and opened up a lively war on the others. As befitting its size, it claimed everything. It introduced Gray as the original inventor of the telephone, and ordered its lawyers to take action at once against the Bell Company for infringement of the Gray patent. This high-handed action, it hoped, would most quickly bring the little Bell group into a humble and submissive frame of mind. Every morning the Western Union looked to see the white flag flying over the Bell headquarters. But no white flag appeared. On the contrary, the news came that the Bell Company had secured two eminent lawyers and were ready to give battle.

    这起案件始于1878年秋季，持续了一年之久，最终却以出人意料的突然结局告终。西联公司的首席律师是乔治·吉福德，他或许是当时最杰出的专利律师。他对专利法了如指掌，随着庭审的进行，他逐渐确信贝尔的专利有效。他私下通知西联公司，他们的诉讼无法成立，“贝尔才是电话的真正发明者”。他建议，最佳策略是撤回诉讼请求并达成和解。这一明智的建议被采纳。第二天，举白旗投降的并非挤在狭小两室办公室里的那群贝尔的拥护者，而是当初傲慢自大的西联公司本身。

    The case began in the Autumn of 1878 and lasted for a year. Then it came to a sudden and most unexpected ending. The lawyer-in-chief of the Western Union was George Gifford, who was perhaps the ablest patent attorney of his day. He was versed in patent lore from Alpha to Omega; and as the trial proceeded, he became convinced that the Bell patent was valid. He notified the Western Union confidentially, of course, that its case could not be proven, and that "Bell was the original inventor of the telephone." The best policy, he suggested, was to withdraw their claims and make a settlement. This wise advice was accepted, and the next day the white flag was hauled up, not by the little group of Bell fighters, who were huddled together in a tiny, two-room office, but by the mighty Western Union itself, which had been so arrogant when the encounter began.

    双方各任命了三名代表组成委员会，经过数月的争论，最终起草并签署了和平条约。根据该条约的条款，西联公司同意——

    A committee of three from each side was appointed, and after months of disputation, a treaty of peace was drawn up and signed. By the terms of this treaty the Western Union agreed--

    （1）承认贝尔是最初的发明者。

    (1) To admit that Bell was the original inventor.

    （2）承认他的专利有效。

    (2) To admit that his patents were valid.

    （3）退出电话行业。

    (3) To retire from the telephone business.

    作为投降的交换条件，贝尔公司同意——

    The Bell Company, in return for this surrender, agreed--

    （1）购买西联电话系统。

    (1) To buy the Western Union telephone system.

    （2）向西联汇款支付所有电话租金的百分之二十的特许权使用费。

    (2) To pay the Western Union a royalty of twenty per cent on all telephone rentals.

    （3）不涉足电报业务。

    (3) To keep out of the telegraph business.

    这份有效期长达十七年的协议，是贝尔公司外交手腕的妙招，堪称电话界的《大宪章》。它将一个强大的竞争对手变成了朋友，为贝尔系统在五十五个城市新增了五万六千部电话，并使这家勇敢的小公司一跃成为行业翘楚，其股价一路飙升，最终突破了每股一千美元的关口。

    This agreement, which was to remain in force for seventeen years, was a master-stroke of diplomacy on the part of the Bell Company. It was the Magna Charta of the telephone. It transformed a giant competitor into a friend. It added to the Bell System fifty-six thousand telephones in fifty-five cities. And it swung the valiant little company up to such a pinnacle of prosperity that its stock went skyrocketing until it touched one thousand dollars a share.

    西联公司败诉的原因很简单：它试图在电报线路上运营电话系统，而这种做法历来都以失败告终；它低估了电话业务的潜力；而且它那些原本就业务繁忙的代理商，既没有时间，也没有知识或热情投入到这项新事业中。即便拥有如此强大的实力，它最终还是败给了这群精挑细选、年轻有为、训练有素且受制于一项几乎无懈可击的专利保护的精英。

    The Western Union had lost its case, for several very simple reasons: It had tried to operate a telephone system on telegraphic lines, a plan that has invariably been unsuccessful, it had a low idea of the possibilities of the telephone business; and its already busy agents had little time or knowledge or enthusiasm to give to the new enterprise. With all its power, it found itself outfought by this compact body of picked men, who were young, zealous, well-handled, and protected by a most invulnerable patent.

    贝尔电话如今与电报、铁路、汽船、收割机以及其他文明国家必需品并驾齐驱。它的开拓时代已经结束。嘲笑和怀疑也随之消失。人人都知道贝尔公司击败了西联公司，纷纷加入到热烈的掌声中。协议签署后不到五个月，公司就不得不进行重组；于是，美国贝尔电话公司成立，注册资本达六百万美元。次年，即1881年，电话线路覆盖了1200个新的城镇，并支付了第一笔股息——178500美元。到了1882年，电话业务迎来了爆发式增长，贝尔系统规模扩大了一倍，总收入超过一百万美元。

    The Bell Telephone now took its place with the Telegraph, the Railroad, the Steamboat, the Harvester, and the other necessities of a civilized country. Its pioneer days were over. There was no more ridicule and incredulity. Every one knew that the Bell people had whipped the West- ern Union, and hastened to join in the grand Te Deum of applause. Within five months from the signing of the agreement, there had to be a reorganization; and the American Bell Telephone Company was created, with six million dollars capital. In the following year, 1881, twelve hundred new towns and cities were marked on the telephone map, and the first dividends were paid --$178,500. And in 1882 there came such a telephone boom that the Bell System was multiplied by two, with more than a million dollars of gross earnings.

    至此，除韦尔之外，所有最早的电话先驱者都退出了历史舞台。托马斯·桑德斯以略低于一百万美元的价格出售了他的股票，不久后又在科罗拉多州的一座金矿中损失了大部分。他的母亲曾是贝尔公司的挚友，如今她的财富翻了一番。加德纳·G·哈伯德退出了商界，但以他那热情洋溢的性格，闲不住，于是他投身于国家地理学会。他就像塞勒斯上校一样，梦想着凭借电话赚得盆满钵满；1897年去世时，他不仅拥有巨额财富，更赢得了朋友们的爱戴。查尔斯·威廉姆斯，第一批电话的制造者，于1881年将他的工厂卖给了贝尔公司，所得金额远超他的预期。与此同时，托马斯·A·沃森也辞职了，他发现自己不再是工薪阶层，而是一位百万富翁。几年后，他在波士顿附近建立了一家造船厂，该厂不断发展壮大，最终雇佣了四千名工人，并为美国海军建造了六艘军舰。

    At this point all the earliest pioneers of the telephone, except Vail, pass out of its history. Thomas Sanders sold his stock for somewhat less than a million dollars, and presently lost most of it in a Colorado gold mine. His mother, who had been so good a friend to Bell, had her fortune doubled. Gardiner G. Hubbard withdrew from business life, and as it was impossible for a man of his ardent temperament to be idle, he plunged into the National Geographical Society. He was a Colonel Sellers whose dream of millions (for the telephone) had come true; and when he died, in 1897, he was rich both in money and in the affection of his friends. Charles Williams, in whose workshop the first telephones were made, sold his factory to the Bell Company in 1881 for more money than he had ever expected to possess. Thomas A. Watson resigned at the same time, finding himself no longer a wage-worker but a millionaire. Several years later he established a shipbuilding plant near Boston, which grew until it employed four thousand workmen and had built half a dozen warships for the United States Navy.

    至于电话行业的创始人贝尔，他做了一个真正的科学波西米亚人会做的事：在结婚当天，他把所有股票都给了新娘，然后继续教聋哑人。恐怕没有哪个国王会送出如此丰厚的结婚礼物；当然，任何国家也没有人像贝尔那样，如此偶然地获得并挥霍了巨额财富。当贝尔公司提出以每年一万美元的薪水邀请他继续担任首席发明家时，他欣然拒绝了，理由是他不能“按订单发明”。1880年，法国政府授予他五万法郎的伏尔塔奖和法国荣誉军团勋章。此后，他获得了许多荣誉，也涉猎广泛。三十年来，他一直是美国公众生活中最杰出、最具传奇色彩的人物之一。但他后来的所有成就，都无法与他28岁时在塞勒姆地下室里所做的一切相提并论。

    As for Bell, the first cause of the telephone business, he did what a true scientific Bohemian might have been expected to do; he gave all his stock to his bride on their marriage-day and resumed his work as an instructor of deaf-mutes. Few kings, if any, had ever given so rich a wedding present; and certainly no one in any country ever obtained and tossed aside an immense fortune as incidentally as did Bell. When the Bell Company offered him a salary of ten thousand dollars a year to remain its chief inventor, he refused the offer cheerfully on the ground that he could not "invent to order." In 1880, the French Government gave him the Volta Prize of fifty thousand francs and the Cross of the Legion of Honor. He has had many honors since then, and many interests. He has been for thirty years one of the most brilliant and picturesque personalities in American public life. But none of his later achievements can in any degree compare with what he did in a cellar in Salem, at twenty-eight years of age.

    这些电话的早期发明者都变得富有，但并非富得流油。当时，乃至此后，都没有人通过出售电话服务成为千万富翁。如果贝尔公司在1880年以最高价出售股票，也只能拿到不到900万美元——这笔钱数额巨大，但对于电话的发明以及一项新兴技术和产业的建立而言，并不算多。这笔钱甚至不及爱荷华州母鸡过去十二个月所产鸡蛋的总价值。

    They had all become rich, these first friends of the telephone, but not fabulously so. There was not at that time, nor has there been since, any one who became a multimillionaire by the sale of telephone service. If the Bell Company had sold its stock at the highest price reached, in 1880, it would have received less than nine million dollars--a huge sum, but not too much to pay for the invention of the telephone and the building up of a new art and a new industry. It was not as much as the value of the eggs laid during the last twelve months by the hens of Iowa.

    但可想而知，当西联公司协议的消息传开后，电话的故事被描绘成一个成功的童话。西奥多·韦尔在华盛顿邮政局的老朋友们为他举办了一场盛宴，并被誉为“电话界的基督山伯爵”。据说，贝尔公司的实际成本仅为其资本的二十五分之一，这意味着每四美分的投资都变成了一美元。就连一向谨慎的杰伊·古尔德也被这些故事冲昏了头脑，跑到纽黑文收购了当地的电话公司，结果后来才发现，该公司的收益竟然低于支出。

    But, as may be imagined, when the news of the Western Union agreement became known, the story of the telephone became a fairy tale of success. Theodore Vail was given a banquet by his old-time friends in the Washington postal service, and toasted as "the Monte Cristo of the Telephone." It was said that the actual cost of the Bell plant was only one-twenty-fifth of its capital, and that every four cents of investment had thus become a dollar. Even Jay Gould, carried beyond his usual caution by these stories, ran up to New Haven and bought its telephone company, only to find out later that its earnings were less than its expenses.

    令贝尔公司大为困惑的是，它很快发现，财富带来的麻烦与贫穷带来的麻烦一样多。一大群推销员和股票投机者蜂拥而至，如同十七年蝗虫般涌向贝尔公司和公众。短短三年内，一百二十五家竞争对手公司横空出世，公然藐视贝尔公司的专利。这些公司的主要目的并非像西联公司那样合法经营电话业务，而是向公众出售股票。它们的股票面值高达2.25亿美元，但其中鲜有公司真正发送过任何信息。一家胆大妄为的公司，既无资金也无专利，竟将其狂妄之举包装成1500万美元的资本。

    Much to the bewilderment of the Bell Company, it soon learned that the troubles of wealth are as numerous as those of poverty. It was beset by a throng of promoters and stock-jobbers, who fell upon it and upon the public like a swarm of seventeen-year locusts. In three years, one hundred and twenty-five competing companies were started, in open defiance of the Bell patents. The main object of these companies was not, like that of the Western Union, to do a legitimate telephone business, but to sell stock to the public. The face value of their stock was $225,000,000, although few of them ever sent a message. One company of unusual impertinence, without money or patents, had capitalized its audacity at $15,000,000.

    如何保住已有的业务——这才是现在的问题。贝尔公司的合伙人没有一个是纯粹的股票投机者。他们甚至一度发誓绝不将任何股票出售给外人。他们以最诚实、最简朴的方式为公司融资；他们坚决反对那些企图将电话业务变成骗局和赌博的金融匪徒。起初，在与西联公司抗衡之后，他们以为可以轻松击败这些股票投机者。但这终究只是一厢情愿。他们发现，这些骗子公司不像西联公司那样公开地进行斗争。

    How to HOLD the business that had been established --that was now the problem. None of the Bell partners had been mere stock-jobbers. At one time they had even taken a pledge not to sell any of their stock to outsiders. They had financed their company in a most honest and simple way; and they were desperately opposed to the financial banditti whose purpose was to transform the telephone business into a cheat and a gamble. At first, having held their own against the Western Union, they expected to make short work of the stock-jobbers. But it was a vain hope. These bogus companies, they found, did not fight in the open, as the Western Union had done.

    各种关于贝尔专利的恶意谣言随即四起。其他发明家——其中一些是诚实的，一些是厚颜无耻的冒牌货——也被拉出来，编造各种离奇的故事，声称自己是先发明者。当时，格兰杰运动在中西部地区是一股强大的政治力量，他们对专利和“垄断”的盲目恐惧被用来猛烈抨击贝尔公司。一些参议员和合法的资本家被推举为这场运动的领军人物。报纸上大肆宣扬“高税率和垄断”，试图转移民众对合法企业与股票公司泡沫之间真正问题的关注。

    All manner of injurious rumors were presently set afloat concerning the Bell patent. Other inventors--some of them honest men, and some shameless pretenders--were brought forward with strangely concocted tales of prior invention. The Granger movement was at that time a strong political factor in the Middle West, and its blind fear of patents and "monopolies" was turned aggressively against the Bell Company. A few Senators and legitimate capitalists were lifted up as the figureheads of the crusade. And a loud hue-and-cry was raised in the newspapers against "high rates and monopoly" to distract the minds of the people from the real issue of legitimate business versus stock-company bubbles.

    在所有觊觎贝尔发明之名的发明家中，最令人信服也最坚持不懈的当属伊莱沙·格雷。他拒绝接受法院的不利判决。败诉数年后，他又祭出新的武器和新的攻击手段。他变得更加敌对和固执；直至1901年去世，他始终坚称自己是电话的原创发明者。

    The most plausible and persistent of all the various inventors who snatched at Bell's laurels, was Elisha Gray. He refused to abide by the adverse decision of the court. Several years after his defeat, he came forward with new weapons and new methods of attack. He became more hostile and irreconcilable; and until his death, in 1901, never renounced his claim to be the original inventor of the telephone.

    这种坚持的原因显而易见。格雷是一位专业的发明家，一位能力超群的人，他从铁匠学徒做起，最终成为奥柏林学院的教授。他一生中凭借专利赚取了超过五百万美元。1874年，他和贝尔在音乐电报的发明竞赛中势均力敌——突然，贝尔凭借其声学知识，转而发明了电话，而格雷则继续紧追不舍。和所有致力于改进电报设备的人一样，格雷也隐约看到了通过电线传输语音的可能性，而巧合的是，就在贝尔提交专利申请的同一天，他也提交了关于这一主题的专利警告。贝尔抢先一步。正如记录簿所示，当天的第五条记录是：“A.G.贝尔，15美元”；第三十九条记录是“E.格雷，10美元”。

    The reason for this persistence is very evident. Gray was a professional inventor, a highly competent man who had begun his career as a blacksmith's apprentice, and risen to be a professor of Oberlin. He made, during his lifetime, over five million dollars by his patents. In 1874, he and Bell were running a neck-and-neck race to see who could first invent a musical telegraph-- when, presto! Bell suddenly turned aside, because of his acoustical knowledge, and invented the telephone, while Gray kept straight ahead. Like all others who were in quest of a better telegraph instrument, Gray had glimmerings of the possibility of sending speech by wire, and by one of the strangest of coincidences he filed a caveat on the subject on the SAME DAY that Bell filed the application for a patent. Bell had arrived first. As the record book shows, the fifth entry on that day was: "A. G. Bell, $15"; and the thirty-ninth entry was "E. Gray, $10."

    格雷的警告声明和贝尔的申请之间存在着巨大的差异。警告声明是作者声明自己尚未发明某物，但相信自己即将发明；而申请声明则是作者声明自己已经完善了该项发明。但格雷始终无法忘记，他一度似乎离最终的胜利如此之近；在被西联公司协议搁置七年后，他带着更加宏大、更加明确的主张再次出现。

    There was a vast difference between Gray's caveat and Bell's application. A caveat is a declaration that the writer has NOT invented a thing, but believes that he is about to do so; while an APPLICATION is a declaration that the writer has already perfected the invention. But Gray could never forget that he had seemed to be, for a time, so close to the golden prize; and seven years after he had been set aside by the Western Union agreement, he reappeared with claims that had grown larger and more definite.

    当仔细梳理格雷诉讼案中的所有证据时，似乎存在三个截然不同的格雷：第一个是嘲讽者格雷，他在百年庆典上考察了贝尔的电话，并称其“不过是老式的情人电报。按照贝尔教授展示的原理，根本不可能制造出实用的通话电话……电流太弱了”；第二个是皈依者格雷，他在1877年坦率地写信给贝尔说：“我并不声称自己是电话的发明者”；第三个是主张者格雷，他在1886年努力证明自己才是电话的真正发明者。他的合伙人伊诺斯·M·巴顿曾巧妙而诙谐地描述过他在这件事上的真实立场：“在所有没有发明电话的人中，格雷是最接近发明电话的人。”

    When all the evidence in the various Gray lawsuits is sifted out, there appear to have been three distinctly different Grays: first, Gray the SCOFFER, who examined Bell's telephone at the Centennial and said it was "nothing but the old lover's telegraph. It is impossible to make a practical speaking telephone on the principle shown by Professor Bell. . . . The currents are too feeble"; second, Gray the CONVERT, who wrote frankly to Bell in 1877, "I do not claim the credit of inventing it"; and third, Gray the CLAIMANT, who endeavored to prove in 1886 that he was the original inventor. His real position in the matter was once well and wittily described by his partner, Enos M. Barton, who said: "Of all the men who DIDN'T invent the telephone, Gray was the nearest."

    现在很明显，电话的发明与格雷没有任何关系。任何国家都没有在使用格雷的电话。格雷本人也承认，正如他在法庭上所承认的那样，他试图按照自己提出的技术方案制造电话，但最终失败了。最近，在华盛顿特区创立电话公司的乔治·C·梅纳德先生对整个事件做出了最终的评价。梅纳德先生说：

    It is now clearly seen that the telephone owes nothing to Gray. There are no Gray telephones in use in any country. Even Gray himself, as he admitted in court, failed when he tried to make a telephone on the lines laid down in his caveat. The final word on the whole matter was recently spoken by George C. Maynard, who established the telephone business in the city of Washington. Said Mr. Maynard:

    “格雷先生是我的挚友，也是我非常珍视的朋友。但恕我直言，在电话问题的某些方面，他的确犯了错误。没有任何一个课题像电话发明那样被研究得如此透彻。没有任何一项专利像贝尔的专利那样遭到四面八方的猛烈攻击；也没有任何一位发明家最终被证明是正确的。贝尔是第一位发明家，格雷并非如此。”

    "Mr. Gray was an intimate and valued friend of mine, but it is no disrespect to his memory to say that on some points involved in the telephone matter, he was mistaken. No subject was ever so thoroughly investigated as the invention of the speaking telephone. No patent has ever been submitted to such determined assault from every direction as Bell's; and no inventor has ever been more completely vindicated. Bell was the first inventor, and Gray was not."

    在格雷之后，对贝尔构成最大挑战的人物是塔夫茨学院的阿莫斯·E·多尔比尔教授。和格雷一样，他也在1877年写信给贝尔表示赞赏。他在信中写道：“先生，我祝贺您这项伟大的发明，我希望它能取代所有现有的电报方式，也希望您能获得应有的财富和荣誉。” 但一年后，多尔比尔带着一部与贝尔的电话出现了。他坚称，这并非贝尔电话的仿制品，而是对德国人菲利普·雷斯于1861年发明的一种电子设备的改进。

    After Gray, the weightiest challenger who came against Bell was Professor Amos E. Dolbear, of Tufts College. He, like Gray, had written a letter of applause to Bell in 1877. "I congratulate you, sir," he said, "upon your very great invention, and I hope to see it supplant all forms of existing telegraphs, and that you will be successful in obtaining the wealth and honor which is your due." But one year later, Dolbear came to view with an opposition telephone. It was not an imitation of Bell's, he insisted, but an improvement upon an electrical device made by a German named Philip Reis, in 1861.

    于是，所谓的“雷斯电话”出现了。从任何实际意义上讲，它根本算不上电话，但在长达九年或更长的时间里，它却成为了对抗贝尔专利的有力武器。可怜的菲利普·雷斯本人，这位德国法兰克福面包师的儿子，曾希望制造出一部真正的电话，但他失败了。他的机器采用“通断式”电流驱动，因此无法传输人声产生的极其细微的振动。它可以传输声音的音调，但无法传输声音的音质。它最多只能传输一段旋律，但永远无法传输一句完整的句子。雷斯在晚年意识到他的机器永远无法用于传输对话；在一封写给朋友的信中，他讲述了自己发明的一种信号编码。

    Thus there appeared upon the scene the so- called "Reis telephone," which was not a telephone at all, in any practical sense, but which served well enough for nine years or more as a weapon to use against the Bell patents. Poor Philip Reis himself, the son of a baker in Frankfort, Germany, had hoped to make a telephone, but he had failed. His machine was operated by a "make-and-break" current, and so could not carry the infinitely delicate vibrations made by the human voice. It could transmit the pitch of a sound, but not the QUALITY. At its best, it could carry a tune, but never at any time a spoken sentence. Reis, in his later years, realized that his machine could never be used for the transmission of conversation; and in a letter to a friend he tells of a code of signals that he has invented.

    贝尔在三年的实验期间，曾制作过一台雷斯电话机，尽管当时他从未见过这种机器。但他很快就把它扔到一边，认为它毫无实用价值。作为一名声学教师，贝尔深知电话必不可少的一点是，它必须能够完整地传输声音，而不仅仅是音调。像开尔文勋爵、约瑟夫·亨利和爱迪生这样的科学家，早在贝尔发明电话之前就见过这种小型雷斯电话机；但他们都认为它不过是个音乐玩具。开尔文勋爵说，它“根本算不上是一部会说话的电话”。爱迪生为了尽可能地为雷斯电话机正名，也曾幽默地承认，当他使用雷斯电话机时，他通常“知道对方要说什么；而且知道对方要说什么，即使是纯粹的雷斯电话机，也能重现出几乎与实际传输的声音一模一样的声音；但当另一端的人不知道对方要说什么时，就很少能听清任何词语了。”

    Bell had once, during his three years of experimenting, made a Reis machine, although at that time he had not seen one. But he soon threw it aside, as of no practical value. As a teacher of acoustics, Bell knew that the one indispensable requirement of a telephone is that it shall transmit the WHOLE of a sound, and not merely the pitch of it. Such scientists as Lord Kelvin, Joseph Henry, and Edison had seen the little Reis instrument years before Bell invented the telephone; but they regarded it as a mere musical toy. It was "not in any sense a speaking telephone," said Lord Kelvin. And Edison, when trying to put the Reis machine in the most favorable light, admitted humorously that when he used a Reis transmitter he generally "knew what was coming; and knowing what was coming, even a Reis transmitter, pure and simple, reproduces sounds which seem almost like that which was being transmitted; but when the man at the other end did not know what was coming, it was very seldom that any word was recognized."

    在多尔贝尔诉讼案中，一台雷斯电话机被带入法庭，引发了不少笑料。它能发出吱吱声，却无法说话。专家和教授们徒劳地尝试，它始终无法发出任何一句清晰可辨的句子。“它能说话，但它就是不说，”多尔贝尔的一位律师解释道。现在人们普遍认为，虽然雷斯电话机在堵塞或故障时能勉强发出一两个词，但它的设计理念是错误的。它根本算不上电话，就像马车算不上雪橇一样，即便可以用链条锁住车轮，让它们滑行一两英尺。洛厄尔法官在他著名的判决中说道：

    In the course of the Dolbear lawsuit, a Reis machine was brought into court, and created much amusement. It was able to squeak, but not to speak. Experts and professors wrestled with it in vain. It refused to transmit one intel- ligible sentence. "It CAN speak, but it WON'T," explained one of Dolbear's lawyers. It is now generally known that while a Reis machine, when clogged and out of order, would transmit a word or two in an imperfect way, it was built on wrong lines. It was no more a telephone than a wagon is a sleigh, even though it is possible to chain the wheels and make them slide for a foot or two. Said Judge Lowell, in rendering his famous decision:

    “即使里斯花费一个世纪的时间，仅仅通过改进结构也无法制造出会说话的电话。贝尔发现，失败的原因并非工艺问题，而是当时所采用的基本原理……贝尔发现了一种新的技术——用电传输语音，而他的成就远不及他的发明本身……追随里斯注定失败；追随贝尔则必将成功。”

    "A century of Reis would never have produced a speaking telephone by mere improvement of construction. It was left for Bell to discover that the failure was due not to workmanship but to the principle which was adopted as the basis of what had to be done. . . . Bell discovered a new art--that of transmitting speech by electricity, and his claim is not as broad as his invention. . . . To follow Reis is to fail; but to follow Bell is to succeed."

    在战胜多尔贝尔之后，贝尔公司的股票一路飙升；股价越高，侵权者和炒作股票泡沫的人就越多。挑拨贝尔公司几乎成了全民运动。任何声称拥有专利权的人，只要编造出任何离奇的发明故事，都能找到投机者支持。形形色色的人蜂拥而至，“有的衣衫褴褛，有的骑着马，有的穿着天鹅绒长袍”。其中一人声称自己在1867年用一个铁环和一把锉刀创造了奇迹；另一人拥有一张玻璃腿的神奇桌子；第三人信誓旦旦地说自己在1860年发明了电话，但直到看到贝尔的专利才知道电话是什么；第四人绘声绘色地讲述了一个故事：1851年，他听到一只牛蛙通过拉到拉辛某个地下室的电报线发出叫声。

    After the victory over Dolbear, the Bell stock went soaring skywards; and the higher it went, the greater were the number of infringers and blowers of stock bubbles. To bait the Bell Company became almost a national sport. Any sort of claimant, with any sort of wild tale of prior invention, could find a speculator to support him. On they came, a motley array, "some in rags, some on nags, and some in velvet gowns." One of them claimed to have done wonders with an iron hoop and a file in 1867; a second had a marvellous table with glass legs; a third swore that he had made a telephone in 1860, but did not know what it was until he saw Bell's patent; and a fourth told a vivid story of having heard a bullfrog croak via a telegraph wire which was strung into a certain cellar in Racine, in 1851.

    这场闹剧在著名的德拉博案中达到了高潮，该案持续了近四年，证据堆积如山，足足有一万页。贝尔的反对者们在德国人赖斯案上败诉后，又推出了一位名叫丹尼尔·德拉博的美国发明家，并展开了一场声势浩大的报纸攻势。为了博取公众对德拉博的同情，他们宣称德拉博在1876年之前就发明了一套完整的电话和交换机，但却“穷困潦倒”，连专利都申请不起。五百名证人接受了质询；这场闹剧引发了轩然大波，迫使贝尔的律师们不得不认真对待这场攻击，并倾尽全力进行反击。

    This comic opera phase came to a head in the famous Drawbaugh case, which lasted for nearly four years, and filled ten thousand pages with its evidence. Having failed on Reis, the German, the opponents of Bell now brought forward an American inventor named Daniel Drawbaugh, and opened up a noisy newspaper campaign. To secure public sympathy for Drawbaugh, it was said that he had invented a complete telephone and switchboard before 1876, but was in such "utter and abject poverty" that he could not get himself a patent. Five hundred witnesses were examined; and such a general turmoil was aroused that the Bell lawyers were compelled to take the attack seriously, and to fight back with every pound of ammunition they possessed.

    德拉博的真实情况是，他曾是宾夕法尼亚州哈里斯堡附近一个乡村的机械师。他心灵手巧，但缺乏创造力；他喜欢在农民和村民面前炫耀自己的机械技艺。他是《科学美国人》杂志的订户；抄袭他人的发明并将其冒充自己的作品，成了他生活中的一个固定习惯。他是个“发明家的搬运工”。在审判中，他被列举了四十多个这种模仿行为，法官严厉地批评了他，指控他“故意捏造事实”。显然，尽管失去了电话发明权，他模仿他人的热情并没有减弱，1903年，他又以“马可尼的搬运工”的身份出现在公众视野中。

    The fact about Drawbaugh is that he was a mechanic in a country village near Harrisburg, Pennsylvania. He was ingenious but not inventive; and loved to display his mechanical skill before the farmers and villagers. He was a subscriber to The Scientific American; and it had become the fixed habit of his life to copy other people's inventions and exhibit them as his own. He was a trailer of inventors. More than forty instances of this imitative habit were shown at the trial, and he was severely scored by the judge, who accused him of "deliberately falsifying the facts." His ruling passion of imitation, apparently, was not diminished by the loss of his telephone claims, as he came to public view again in 1903 as a trailer of Marconi.

    德拉博的败诉再次推高了贝尔公司的股价，同时也引来了一支自称“陆路公司”的强大反抗力量。这家公司发现，没有任何一个索赔者能在法庭上击败贝尔，于是便将败诉者们聚集起来，兜售一堆杂乱无章的专利。几位实力雄厚的资本家承诺承担这项冒险行动的费用。他们架设了电线，出售了股票，一切看起来都那么真实可信，以至于当贝尔公司的律师申请禁令时，遭到了拒绝。这是贝尔公司在长达十一年的诉讼中遭受的最沉重的打击；贝尔公司的股价在短短几天内暴跌了35点。侵权公司如雨后春笋般涌现。一切都进行得很顺利，直到 Overland 公司被法院驳回，因为除了“以前案件的残渣和残余——在嬉戏结束时在杯子里发现的鞋跟敲击器”之外，没有任何证据。

    Drawbaugh's defeat sent the Bell stock up once more, and brought on a Xerxes' army of opposition which called itself the "Overland Company." Having learned that no one claim- ant could beat Bell in the courts, this company massed the losers together and came forward with a scrap-basket full of patents. Several powerful capitalists undertook to pay the expenses of this adventure. Wires were strung; stock was sold; and the enterprise looked for a time so genuine that when the Bell lawyers asked for an injunction against it, they were refused. This was as hard a blow as the Bell people received in their eleven years of litigation; and the Bell stock tumbled thirty-five points in a few days. Infringing companies sprang up like gourds in the night. And all went merrily with the promoters until the Overland Company was thrown out of court, as having no evidence, except "the refuse and dregs of former cases-- the heel-taps found in the glasses at the end of the frolic."

    但即便索赔方败诉，这场闹剧也并未就此结束。他们接下来计划通过政治手段来获取法律无法实现的目标；他们诱使政府提起诉讼，要求撤销贝尔的专利。这是一个大胆而孤注一掷的举动，使得纸业公司的发起人得以继续销售股票数年之久。整个争端从格雷到德拉博，被重新提起。每一场战斗都被重新打响；最终，政府官员们当然明白，他们只是被利用来从火堆中捞取电话专利而已。此案最终不了了之，于1896年非正式地被撤销。

    But even after this defeat for the claimants, the frolic was not wholly ended. They next planned to get through politics what they could not get through law; they induced the Government to bring suit for the annulment of the Bell patents. It was a bold and desperate move, and enabled the promoters of paper companies to sell stock for several years longer. The whole dispute was re-opened, from Gray to Drawbaugh. Every battle was re-fought; and in the end, of course, the Government officials learned that they were being used to pull telephone chestnuts out of the fire. The case was allowed to die a natural death, and was informally dropped in 1896.

    贝尔公司总共打赢了十三起具有全国意义的诉讼，其中五起上诉至华盛顿最高法院。此外，它还打赢了五百八十七起其他各种性质的诉讼；除了两起无关紧要的合同诉讼外，它从未败诉。

    In all, the Bell Company fought out thirteen lawsuits that were of national interest, and five that were carried to the Supreme Court in Washington. It fought out five hundred and eighty- seven other lawsuits of various natures; and with the exception of two trivial contract suits, IT NEVER LOST A CASE.

    它的经历无可辩驳地控诉了我们保护发明人的制度。没有哪个发明家比贝尔拥有更清晰的专利权。1884年，专利局对所有电话专利进行了长达18个月的调查，并报告称：“世界拥有会说话的电话要归功于贝尔。”然而，他的专利却一直饱受争议，从未真正稳固过。一些资本总额超过5亿美元的股份公司成立，试图打破他的专利；从始至终，电话的成功与其说是建立在专利垄断之上，不如说是建立在一个组织完善的商业体系之上。

    Its experience is an unanswerable indictment of our system of protecting inventors. No inventor had ever a clearer title than Bell. The Patent Office itself, in 1884, made an eighteen- months' investigation of all telephone patents, and reported: "It is to Bell that the world owes the possession of the speaking telephone." Yet his patent was continuously under fire, and never at any time secure. Stock companies whose paper capital totalled more than $500,000,000 were organized to break it down; and from first to last the success of the telephone was based much less upon the monopoly of patents than upon the building up of a well organized business.

    幸运的是，贝尔和支持他的人有两位律师大师为他们辩护，这两位大师在团队合作和效率方面几乎无人能及——他们分别是昌西·史密斯和詹姆斯·J·斯托罗。这两人配合得天衣无缝。史密斯是一位韦伯斯特式的传统律师，举止庄重，沉稳有力，令人印象深刻。到了1878年，当他受邀为规模不大的贝尔公司辩护，对抗实力雄厚的西部联合公司时，史密斯已成为波士顿最著名的专利律师。他身材魁梧，体格健壮，让人想起本杰明·富兰克林，脸上刮得干干净净，留着一头长发，发梢微卷，身穿燕尾服，高领，头戴海狸皮帽。

    Fortunately for Bell and the men who upheld him, they were defended by two master-lawyers who have seldom, if ever, had an equal for team work and efficiency--Chauncy Smith and James J. Storrow. These two men were marvellously well mated. Smith was an old-fashioned attorney of the Websterian sort, dignified, ponderous, and impressive. By 1878, when he came in to defend the little Bell Company against the towering Western Union, Smith had become the most noted patent lawyer in Boston. He was a large, thick-set man, a reminder of Benjamin Franklin, with clean-shaven face, long hair curling at the ends, frock coat, high collar, and beaver hat.

    斯托罗则恰恰相反，他身材矮小，举止沉稳，辩论时语气温和，而且知识渊博，堪称一本活的百科全书。他做事极其严谨，以至于成为贝尔公司的律师后，他首先在彼得舍姆的乡间别墅里待了一个夏天，潜心研究物理和电学定律。他为人低调，从不张扬。在长达十一年的诉讼过程中，他只失控过一次。当时他正在质疑一位证人的可信度，这位证人是他安排出庭作证的，但却被对方律师篡改了证词。“但这可是你们自己的证人啊！”对方律师抗议道。“没错！”平时说话轻声细语的斯托罗大声喊道，“他曾经是我的证人，但现在他成了你们的骗子！”

    Storrow, on the contrary, was a small man, quiet in manner, conversational in argument, and an encyclopedia of definite information. He was so thorough that, when he became a Bell lawyer, he first spent an entire summer at his country home in Petersham, studying the laws of physics and electricity. He was never in the slightest degree spectacular. Once only, during the eleven years of litigation, did he lose control of his temper. He was attacking the credibility of a witness whom he had put on the stand, but who had been tampered with by the opposition lawyers. "But this man is your own witness," protested the lawyers. "Yes," shouted the usually soft-speaking Storrow; "he WAS my witness, but now he is YOUR LIAR."

    这两位男士的效率因第三位成员的加入而大大提升——托马斯·D·洛克伍德，他于1879年被韦尔选中，负责建立专利部门。两年前，洛克伍德在纽约奇克林大厅听过贝尔的演讲，当时他还是个“怀疑论者”。但对电话的深入研究让他彻底成为了电话的拥护者。洛克伍德记忆力惊人，极具发明才能，因此非常适合创建这样一个部门。他简直就是为这个职位而生的。在他的领导下，电气专利的数量从1878年的几百项增长到1910年的八万项。

    The efficiency of these two men was greatly increased by a third--Thomas D. Lockwood, who was chosen by Vail in 1879 to establish a Patent Department. Two years before, Lockwood had heard Bell lecture in Chickering Hall, New York, and was a "doubting Thomas." But a closer study of the telephone transformed him into an enthusiast. Having a memory like a filing system, and a knack for invention, Lockwood was well fitted to create such a depart- ment. He was a man born for the place. And he has seen the number of electrical patents grow from a few hundred in 1878 to eighty thousand in 1910.

    这三位是贝尔专利的捍卫者。在韦尔建立起新兴的电话业务的过程中，他们力挽狂澜，使其免遭投机性竞争的摧残。史密斯制定了全面的辩护方案。凭借他的睿智和经验，他能够阐明贝尔有权据以辩护的总体原则。通常情况下，他负责结案陈词，而且他的陈述极具说服力，他会用低沉的声音慷慨陈词：“法官阁下，我认为，在贝尔先生获得专利之前，世界上没有任何文献记载过人声是如何通过电信号传输的。”他的死，如同他的一生，充满戏剧性。当时他正站在法庭上，与侵权者激烈辩论，却在陈述到一半时，突然倒地，病痛缠身，十二年来肩负的责任也让他不堪重负。斯托罗则以另一种方式发挥了与史密斯同样不可或缺的作用。正是他搭建了贝尔辩护的框架。他是一位精于细节的大师。他头脑敏锐，思维犀利；只要电话技术存在，他的一些简报就会被人研究。在行动中，他堪比一挺速射加特林机枪；而史密斯则像一门百吨重的大炮，洛克伍德则是炮弹的制造者。

    These three men were the defenders of the Bell patents. As Vail built up the young telephone business, they held it from being torn to shreds in an orgy of speculative competition. Smith prepared the comprehensive plan of defence. By his sagacity and experience he was enabled to mark out the general principles upon which Bell had a right to stand. Usually, he closed the case, and he was immensely effective as he would declaim, in his deep voice: "I submit, Your Honor, that the literature of the world does not afford a passage which states how the human voice can be electrically transmitted, previous to the patent of Mr. Bell." His death, like his life, was dramatic. He was on his feet in the courtroom, battling against an infringer, when, in the middle of a sentence, he fell to the floor, overcome by sickness and the responsibilities he had carried for twelve years. Storrow, in a different way, was fully as indispensable as Smith. It was he who built up the superstructure of the Bell defence. He was a master of details. His brain was keen and incisive; and some of his briefs will be studied as long as the art of telephony exists. He might fairly have been compared, in action, to a rapid-firing Gatling gun; while Smith was a hundred-ton cannon, and Lockwood was the maker of the ammunition.

    史密斯和斯托罗提出了三个主要论点，这些论点从未被驳倒，也永远不可能被驳倒。当时五十多位最杰出的律师试图推翻这些论点，但都失败了。第一个论点是贝尔清晰明了地讲述了他是如何发明电话的，这驳斥并驳斥了那些冒名顶替者。第二个论点是历史事实：欧洲和美国最杰出的电子科学家在百年庆典上亲眼目睹了贝尔的电话，并宣布它是全新的——“不仅是全新的，而且是奇妙的，”廷德尔说道。第三个论点是极其重要的事实：在贝尔的专利获得十七个月后，才有人质疑他自称是电话的原创发明者。

    Smith and Storrow had three main arguments that never were, and never could be, answered. Fifty or more of the most eminent lawyers of that day tried to demolish these arguments, and failed. The first was Bell's clear, straightforward story of HOW HE DID IT, which rebuked and confounded the mob of pretenders. The second was the historical fact that the most eminent electrical scientists of Europe and America had seen Bell's telephone at the Centennial and had declared it to be NEW--"not only new but marvellous," said Tyndall. And the third was the very significant fact that no one challenged Bell's claim to be the original inventor of the telephone until his patent was seventeen months old.

    这项专利本身也是一份非凡的文件。它如同贝尔公司的一道安全屏障。十一年来，它饱受四面八方的攻击，却从未动摇。它涵盖了一整门技术，却在其整个生命周期中都屹立不倒。如果全文印刷，这本书就占了十页；但其核心内容却在最后一句话：“一种通过产生类似于伴随所述声音的空气振动的电波波动，以电报方式传输语音或其他声音的方法和装置。” 这几句话表达了一个前所未有的想法。它无可辩驳，也无法被推翻。虽然只有短短三十二个字，但在六年时间里，这三个字却代表着每字一百万美元的投资。

    The patent itself, too, was a remarkable document. It was a Gibraltar of security to the Bell Company. For eleven years it was attacked from all sides, and never dented. It covered an entire art, yet it was sustained during its whole lifetime. Printed in full, it would make ten pages of this book; but the core of it is in the last sentence: "The method of, and apparatus for, transmitting vocal or other sounds telegraphically, by causing electrical undulations, similar in form to the vibrations of the air accompanying the said vocal or other sounds." These words expressed an idea that had never been written before. It could not be evaded or overcome. There were only thirty-two words, but in six years these words represented an investment of a million dollars apiece.

    如今，这场伟大的专利大战的喧嚣已然平息，贝尔所获得的荣誉和回报显然与他应得的完全一致。在他发明电话之前，世上根本没有电话；而自从他发明电话以来，再也没有人找到其他的电话制造方法。三十多年来，成百上千的聪明人试图超越贝尔，然而，世界上所有的电话仍然沿用贝尔发明的原理。

    Now that the clamor of this great patent war has died away, it is evident that Bell received no more credit and no more reward than he deserved. There was no telephone until he made one, and since he made one, no one has found out any other way. Hundreds of clever men have been trying for more than thirty years to outrival Bell, and yet every telephone in the world is still made on the plan that Bell discovered.

    在贝尔之前，没有任何一位发明家对电话的发明贡献能比得上间接帮助贝尔，正如弗拉·毛罗和托斯卡内利绘制地图和海图帮助哥伦布发现美洲一样。贝尔的父亲教会了他声学定律；亥姆霍兹教会了他磁铁对声波振动的影响；柯尼希和莱昂·斯科特教会了他这些振动的无穷多样性；克拉伦斯·J·布莱克博士让他拥有了用于实验的人耳；约瑟夫·亨利和查尔斯·惠斯通爵士鼓励他坚持不懈。此外，莫尔斯发明的电报、法拉第发现的磁感应现象、斯特金的第一块电磁铁以及伏打的电池也以更为间接的方式帮助了他。从伽利略、牛顿到富兰克林、西蒙·纽科姆，科学家们取得的所有成就，都从总体上帮助了贝尔，因为它们营造了一种科学氛围和思维习惯。但在电话的实际制造过程中，贝尔之前和之后都无人能及。他是第一个发明电话的人，而且是独自一人完成的。

    No inventor who preceded Bell did more, in the invention of the telephone, than to help Bell indirectly, in the same way that Fra Mauro and Toscanelli helped in the discovery of America by making the map and chart that were used by Columbus. Bell was helped by his father, who taught him the laws of acoustics; by Helmholtz, who taught him the influence of magnets upon sound vibrations; by Koenig and Leon Scott, who taught him the infinite variety of these vibrations; by Dr. Clarence J. Blake, who gave him a human ear for his experiments; and by Joseph Henry and Sir Charles Wheatstone, who encouraged him to persevere. In a still more indirect way, he was helped by Morse's invention of the telegraph; by Faraday's discovery of the phenomena of magnetic induction; by Sturgeon's first electro-magnet; and by Volta's electric battery. All that scientists had achieved, from Galileo and Newton to Franklin and Simon Newcomb, helped Bell in a general way, by creat- ing a scientific atmosphere and habit of thought. But in the actual making of the telephone, there was no one with Bell nor before him. He invented it first, and alone.

    第四章 艺术的发展

    CHAPTER IV. THE DEVELOPMENT OF THE ART

    电话诞生之时，已有四项使用电线的业务在运营：火警、防盗、电报和信使服务。起初，不出所料，不起眼的电话也和其他这些业务一样，被边缘化了。对普通大众而言，它不过是个科学玩具；但在这些架设电线的行业里，有少数人看到了发展电话业务的曙光。他们把电话安装在当时使用的电线上。随着电话的普及，他们又增加了电话的数量。每个客户都希望能够与其他人通话。于是，在开始提供电话服务后，他们很快发现自己正面临着现代最复杂、最令人费解的工程难题——如何围绕电话设计一种能够实现普遍服务的机制。

    Four wire-using businesses were already in the field when the telephone was born: the fire-alarm, burglar-alarm, telegraph, and messenger- boy service; and at first, as might have been expected, the humble little telephone was huddled in with these businesses as a sort of poor relation. To the general public, it was a mere scientific toy; but there were a few men, not many, in these wire-stringing trades, who saw a glimmering chance of creating a telephone business. They put telephones on the wires that were then in use. As these became popular, they added others. Each of their customers wished to be able to talk to every one else. And so, having undertaken to give telephone service, they presently found themselves battling with the most intricate and baffling engineering problem of modern times--the construction around the tele- phone of such a mechanism as would bring it into universal service.

    这些人中第一个是托马斯·A·沃森，这位年轻的机械师受雇于贝尔，担任他的助手。他开创的事业，如今需要两万六千人才能完成。在几年时间里，他几乎包揽了电话公司的全部工程和制造工作，到1880年，他已经凭借自己的发明获得了六十项专利。贝尔最初设计的电话简直像个玩具，振膜极其脆弱，连一阵温热的呼吸都会让它失灵。沃森接手后，将其改造成了一台更加坚固耐用的机器。贝尔最初使用的是一块脆弱的金箔圆盘，中间粘着一块铁片。起初，他难以置信一块纯铁圆盘竟然会在说话的轻微作用下振动。但他和沃森发现，当铁片面积增大时，通话质量会更好。不久之后，他们便弃用了金箔，只使用铁片。

    The first of these men was Thomas A. Watson, the young mechanic who had been hired as Bell's helper. He began a work that to-day requires an army of twenty-six thousand people. He was for a couple of years the total engineering and manufacturing department of the telephone business, and by 1880 had taken out sixty patents for his own suggestions. It was Watson who took the telephone as Bell had made it, really a toy, with its diaphragm so delicate that a warm breath would put it out of order, and toughened it into a more rugged machine. Bell had used a disc of fragile gold-beaters' skin with a patch of sheet-iron glued to the centre. He could not believe, for a time, that a disc of all-iron would vibrate under the slight influence of a spoken word. But he and Watson noticed that when the patch was bigger the talking was better, and presently they threw away the gold-beaters' skin and used the iron alone.

    此外，沃森还花了数月时间试验各种尺寸的铁片，以找到最能有效传递声音的铁片。他发现，如果铁片太厚，声音就会像木偶戏里的尖叫一样刺耳；如果太薄，声音就会变成空洞而阴森的呻吟，仿佛说话者的头伸进了桶里。他们还花了几个月的时间来确定铁片前方空气腔的合适尺寸和形状。因此，电话在原理上已经完善之后，又花了一整年的时间才将其从科学玩具的范畴中解放出来，之后又花了一两年的时间才将其正式推向商业领域。

    Also, it was Watson who spent months experimenting with all sorts and sizes of iron discs, so as to get the one that would best convey the sound. If the iron was too thick, he discovered, the voice was shrilled into a Punch-and-Judy squeal; and if it was too thin, the voice became a hollow and sepulchral groan, as if the speaker had his head in a barrel. Other months, too, were spent in finding out the proper size and shape for the air cavity in front of the disc. And so, after the telephone had been perfected, IN PRINCIPLE, a full year was required to lift it out of the class of scientific toys, and another year or two to present it properly to the business world.

    直到1878年，贝尔电话公司的所有电话设备都是由沃森在波士顿法院街查尔斯·威廉姆斯的小作坊里生产的——那栋建筑早已改建成一家五分钱的剧院。但业务很快发展壮大，小作坊已无法满足需求。订单积压了五周之久。代理商们焦头烂额，忧心忡忡。必须迅速采取行动，于是贝尔公司向其他四家制造商颁发了生产电话铃、交换机等设备的许可证。与此同时，芝加哥的西部电气公司也开始为西部联合公司生产侵权的格雷-爱迪生电话，因此很快就有六组技工在为这种新型通话设备绞尽脑汁。

    Until 1878 all Bell telephone apparatus was made by Watson in Charles Williams's little shop in Court Street, Boston--a building long since transformed into a five-cent theatre. But the business soon grew too big for the shop. Orders fell five weeks behind. Agents stormed and fretted. Some action had to be taken quickly, so licenses were given to four other manufacturers to make bells, switchboards, and so forth. By this time the Western Electric Company of Chicago had begun to make the infringing Gray-Edison telephones for the Western Union, so that there were soon six groups of mechanics puzzling their wits over the new talk-machinery.

    到1880年，电话设备的产量已经相当可观，但种类繁多，令人眼花缭乱。就好比当年的夏装款式繁多，设计花哨。如果想要实现某种程度的统一，下一步显然是收购并合并这六家公司；到1881年，韦尔公司就完成了这项收购。这是电话史上第一次合并，意义极其重大。如果没有这一举措，电话行业很可能就会因为竞争对手之间的内战而分崩离析。

    By 1880 there was plenty of telephonic apparatus being made, but in too many different varieties. Not all the summer gowns of that year presented more styles and fancies. The next step, if there was to be any degree of uniformity, was plainly to buy and consolidate these six companies; and by 1881 Vail had done this. It was the first merger in telephone history. It was a step of immense importance. Had it not been taken, the telephone business would have been torn into fragments by the civil wars between rival inventors.

    从那时起，西电公司就成了电话设备的总部。它是名副其实的“大本营”，所有道路都通向它。无论新想法诞生于何处，迟早都会来到西电公司，寻求将其转化为实物。这里汇聚了后来成为电话行业核心的熟练工匠。同时，这里也聚集了许多杰出的发明家和工程师，他们为现代电缆和交换机的发展做出了卓越贡献。

    From this time the Western Electric became the headquarters of telephonic apparatus. It was the Big Shop, all roads led to it. No matter where a new idea was born, sooner or later it came knocking at the door of the Western Electric to receive a material body. Here were the skilled workmen who became the hands of the telephone business. And here, too, were many of the ablest inventors and engineers, who did most to develop the cables and switchboards of to-day.

    1882年，沃森从波士顿辞职。一两年后，一位名叫E·T·吉利兰的新人及时出现，接替了他的位置。这位杰出人物对电话行业来说可谓雪中送炭。他原本是印第安纳波利斯的一位电器制造商，直到韦尔的整合政策将他纳入了先驱者和开拓者的核心群体。在接下来的五年里，吉利兰引领潮流，致力于开发更好、更便宜的设备。他充分利用了当时极其困难的局面。他如此能干，如此足智多谋，总能找到办法解决困扰早期电话代理商的机械难题，而且无需他们投入大量资金。他利用当时已有的理念和设备，帮助电话行业度过了最关键的时期——那时几乎没有时间和资金进行实验。例如，他以电报的插销式交换机为蓝本，将其发展到了极致，达到了当时无人能及的境界。它是当时最实用、最完善的交换机，在被更为复杂、昂贵的现代交换机取代之前，一直占据着市场主导地位。

    In Boston, Watson had resigned in 1882, and in his place, a year or two later stood a timely new arrival named E. T. Gilliland. This really notable man was a friend in need to the telephone. He had been a manufacturer of electrical apparatus in Indianapolis, until Vail's policy of consolidation drew him into the central group of pioneers and pathfinders. For five years Gilliland led the way as a developer of better and cheaper equipment. He made the best of a most difficult situation. He was so handy, so resourceful, that he invariably found a way to unravel the mechanical tangles that perplexed the first telephone agents, and this, too, without compelling them to spend large sums of capital. He took the ideas and apparatus that were then in existence, and used them to carry the telephone business through the most critical period of its life, when there was little time or money to risk on experiments. He took the peg switchboard of the telegraph, for in- stance, and developed it to its highest point, to a point that was not even imagined possible by any one else. It was the most practical and complete switchboard of its day, and held the field against all comers until it was superseded by the modern type of board, vastly more elaborate and expensive.

    到1884年，在波士顿的吉利兰和芝加哥的西部电气公司周围，聚集了一群机械师和高中毕业生，他们大多非常年轻，没什么名声可言；他们一部分是为了谋生，一部分是出于兴趣，一头扎进了这个当时历史尚浅、声望也低的新兴行业。这些年轻的冒险家，其中大多数人至今仍然健在，成为了工业史的缔造者。毫无疑问，他们是现代电话工程这门科学的奠基人。

    By 1884, gathered around Gilliland in Boston and the Western Electric in Chicago, there came to be a group of mechanics and high-school graduates, very young men, mostly, who had no reputations to lose; and who, partly for a living and mainly for a lark, plunged into the difficulties of this new business that had at that time little history and less prestige. These young adventurers, most of whom are still alive, became the makers of industrial history. They were unquestionably the founders of the present science of telephone engineering.

    他们轻率地迎难而上，却发现这个问题远比他们想象的要复杂得多。这简直是不可能完成的任务。表面上看，这简直是一场噩梦般的壮举——要编织一张错综复杂的电线网，让每部电话都能与其他所有电话连接起来。书籍和大学都帮不上他们的忙。沃森虽然略懂一些相关知识，却成了一名造船工人。电气工程这门职业当时还未出现。至于他们的电报经验，虽然在一段时间内确实有所帮助，但却让他们走上了错误的道路，做了许多事后不得不纠正的错误。

    The problem that they dashed at so lightheartedly was much larger than any of them imagined. It was a Gibraltar of impossibilities. It was on the face of it a fantastic nightmare of a task--to weave such a web of wires, with in- terlocking centres, as would put any one telephone in touch with every other. There was no help for them in books or colleges. Watson, who had acquired a little knowledge, had become a shipbuilder. Electrical engineering, as a profession, was unborn. And as for their telegraphic experience, while it certainly helped them for a time, it started them in the wrong direction and led them to do many things which had afterwards to be undone.

    这些年轻探路者所面对的奇特电流，或许是世上速度最快、最微弱、最难以捉摸的力量。它如此神奇，以至于任何描述都显得不合常理。它像婴儿的阳光般温柔，又像闪电般迅疾。它的电流如此微弱，一盏白炽灯的电流竟比它大五亿倍。只需将一勺热水冷却一度，冷却释放的能量就足以让一部电话运行一万年。接住孩子落下的泪珠，就能获得足够的水力，将语音信息从一座城市传递到另一座城市。

    The peculiar electric current that these young pathfinders had to deal with is perhaps the quickest, feeblest, and most elusive force in the world. It is so amazing a thing that any description of it seems irrational. It is as gentle as a touch of a baby sunbeam, and as swift as the lightning flash. It is so small that the electric current of a single incandescent lamp is greater 500,000,000 times. Cool a spoonful of hot water just one degree, and the energy set free by the cooling will operate a telephone for ten thousand years. Catch the falling tear-drop of a child, and there will be sufficient water-power to carry a spoken message from one city to another.

    这就是那小小的电线精灵，它需要被保护和训练才能服从。它是所有电子精灵中最弱小的一个，却有着数不清的敌人。敌人！这世界到处都是它的敌人。有闪电，它的兄长，用致命的打击攻击它。有电报电流和光电流，它强大而恶毒的表亲，只要它靠近，就会追逐并攻击它。有雨、雨夹雪、雪以及各种各样的潮湿，都在伺机掳走它。有河流、树木和尘埃。似乎所有已知和未知的自然力量都在合谋阻挠或消灭这个由亚历山大·格雷厄姆·贝尔的魔法创造出来的温柔的小信使。

    Such is the tiny Genie of the Wire that had to be protected and trained into obedience. It was the most defenceless of all electric sprites, and it had so many enemies. Enemies! The world was populous with its enemies. There was the lightning, its elder brother, striking at it with murderous blows. There were the telegraphic and light-and-power currents, its strong and malicious cousins, chasing and assaulting it whenever it ventured too near. There were rain and sleet and snow and every sort of moisture, lying in wait to abduct it. There were rivers and trees and flecks of dust. It seemed as if all the known and unknown agencies of nature were in conspiracy to thwart or annihilate this gentle little messenger who had been conjured into life by the wizardry of Alexander Graham Bell.

    这些年轻人从贝尔和沃森那里得到的，仅仅是电话里我们称之为听筒的那部分。这几乎就是贝尔发明的全部，而且至今仍保持着他最初的设计。在当时，它是，而且现在仍然是任何国家投入使用的最灵敏的仪器。它开启了一个全新的声音世界。它能回荡苍蝇走过桌子的脚步声，或者在新奥尔良重现纽约孩童的咿呀学语。这就是这些年轻人得到的，仅此而已。当时没有任何像样的交换机，没有任何有价值的电缆，没有任何合格的线路，没有任何测试或信号理论，没有任何交换机，没有任何形式的电话系统。

    All that these young men had received from Bell and Watson was that part of the telephone that we call the receiver. This was practically the sum total of Bell's invention, and remains to-day as he made it. It was then, and is yet, the most sensitive instrument that has ever been put to general use in any country. It opened up a new world of sound. It would echo the tramp of a fly that walked across a table, or repeat in New Orleans the prattle of a child in New York. This was what the young men received, and this was all. There were no switchboards of any account, no cables of any value, no wires that were in any sense adequate, no theory of tests or signals, no exchanges, NO TELEPHONE SYSTEM OF ANY SORT WHATEVER.

    贝尔最初的电话线就像晾衣绳一样简单。每根短小的电线独立存在，两端各连接一台设备。当时没有接线员、交换机或交换台。但如今，需要多人同时通话的情况已经出现。这标志着电话用途的扩展；虽然贝尔本人预见到了这一点，但他并没有制定出相应的实施方案。于是，一个全新的、极其艰巨的问题摆在了眼前——如何将三部电话、三百部电话、三千部电话，甚至三百万部电话连接起来，以便随时将任意两部电话连接起来。

    As for Bell's first telephone lines, they were as simple as clothes-lines. Each short little wire stood by itself, with one instrument at each end. There were no operators, switchboards, or exchanges. But there had now come a time when more than two persons wanted to be in the same conversational group. This was a larger use of the telephone; and while Bell himself had foreseen it, he had not worked out a plan whereby it could be carried out. Here was the new problem, and a most stupendous one--how to link together three telephones, or three hundred, or three thousand, or three million, so that any two of them could be joined at a moment's notice.

    但这还不是全部。这些年轻人不仅要与神秘力量和“空中力量”作斗争；不仅要保护他们那小小的电子信使，还要建造一套电线系统，让他可以安全地在上面来回穿梭；他们要做的远不止这些。他们必须让这套系统简单易用，万无一失，让除了聋哑人以外的所有人，都能在没有任何经验的情况下轻松上手。他们必须训练贝尔的电线精灵，让他不仅服从主人的命令，还要服从任何人的命令——任何能用任何语言与他交流的人。

    And that was not all. These young men had not only to battle against mystery and "the powers of the air"; they had not only to protect their tiny electric messenger, and to create a system of wire highways along which he could run up and down safely; they had to do more. They had to make this system so simple and fool-proof that every one--every one except the deaf and dumb--could use it without any previous experience. They had to educate Bell's Genie of the Wire so that he would not only obey his masters, but anybody--anybody who could speak to him in any language.

    毫无疑问，如果这些年轻人停下来仔细思考一下他们​​毕生的事业，有些人或许会选择放弃。但他们没有时间去想那么多。他们就像被推入深水才学会游泳的孩子。电话业务一旦起步，就必须持续发展；随着业务的增长，各种瓶颈接踵而至。摆在他们面前的是两条路：要么为了适应设备而限制业务发展，要么发展设备以跟上业务的步伐。电话公司的大部分人选择了发展；而那些后来让他们名声大噪的杰出发明，正是出于无奈和绝望的驱使。

    No doubt, if the young men had stopped to consider their life-work as a whole, some of them might have turned back. But they had no time to philosophize. They were like the boy who learns how to swim by being pushed into deep water. Once the telephone business was started, it had to be kept going; and as it grew, there came one after another a series of congestions. Two courses were open; either the business had to be kept down to suit the apparatus, or the apparatus had to be developed to keep pace with the business. The telephone men, most of them, at least, chose development; and the brilliant inventions that afterwards made some of them famous were compelled by sheer necessity and desperation.

    贝尔发明之后第一个显著的改进是埃米尔·贝利纳于1877年制造的发射机。这同样是一段传奇。贝利纳十九岁时，还是个贫穷的德国青年，1870年来到卡斯尔花园，希望能闯出一番天地。他自述在纽约一家化学品商店找到了一份“每周六美元的洗瓶工”的工作。晚上，他会在库珀联盟学院的免费课程中学习科学。后来，一位名叫恩格尔的药剂师送给他一本穆勒的物理学著作，这本书恰好激发了他的创造力。1876年，他对电话着迷，并着手按照不同的方案制造电话。几个月后，他成功了，并欣喜若狂地获得了他的第一项电话发射机专利。此时，他已经从洗瓶工的岗位上晋升为华盛顿一家杂货店的店员；但他仍然很穷，而且像大多数发明家一样，缺乏实际行动。美国科学界的贤哲约瑟夫·亨利是他的朋友，但年事已高，无力提供任何帮助。因此，当爱迪生两周后也发明了发射机时，贝利纳的先例一度被完全忽略。后来，贝尔公司买下了贝利纳的专利，并站在他这边。此后，案件经历了漫长而令人恼火的拖延——长达十四年之久——最终，美国最高法院裁定，发射机的真正发明者是贝利纳，而非爱迪生。

    The first notable improvement upon Bell's invention was the making of the transmitter, in 1877, by Emile Berliner. This, too, was a romance. Berliner, as a poor German youth of nineteen, had landed in Castle Garden in 1870 to seek his fortune. He got a job as "a sort of bottle-washer at six dollars a week," he says, in a chemical shop in New York. At nights he studied science in the free classes of Cooper Union. Then a druggist named Engel gave him a copy of Muller's book on physics, which was precisely the stimulus needed by his creative brain. In 1876 he was fascinated by the telephone, and set out to construct one on a different plan. Several months later he had succeeded and was overjoyed to receive his first patent for a telephone transmitter. He had by this time climbed up from his bottle-washing to be a clerk in a drygoods store in Washington; but he was still poor and as unpractical as most in- ventors. Joseph Henry, the Sage of the American scientific world, was his friend, though too old to give him any help. Consequently, when Edison, two weeks later, also invented a transmitter, the prior claim of Berliner was for a time wholly ignored. Later the Bell Company bought Berliner's patent and took up his side of the case. There was a seemingly endless succession of delays--fourteen years of the most vexatious delays--until finally the Supreme Court of the United States ruled that Berliner, and not Edison, was the original inventor of the transmitter.

    从最初到现在，发射器的发明凝聚了众多智慧。其基本原理是通过改变两点间的压力来改变电流。贝尔在其著名的专利中无疑提出了这一概念，他写道：“增加和减少电阻”。伯林纳是第一个真正制造出发射器的人。爱迪生用柔软的碳棒代替钢棒，极大地改进了发射器。肯塔基州的一位教授大卫·E·休斯开创了新的发展方向，他将贝尔电话改造成“麦克风”，这是一种神奇的小仪器，可以探测到苍蝇走过桌子时发出的声音。波士顿的弗朗西斯·布莱克将麦克风改​​造成了实用的发射器。英国牧师亨利·亨宁斯想到了使用碳颗粒作为电极的妙招。贝尔公司的专家之一怀特对亨宁斯设计的发射器进行了改进，使其成为现在的样子。如今，发射器和接收器似乎已经达到了人类智慧所能达到的最完美的人工耳蜗和舌头。它们不断变得越来越复杂，以至于今天放在桌子上的电话机包含多达一百三十个独立部件，以及一勺闪闪发光的碳颗粒。

    From first to last, the transmitter has been the product of several minds. Its basic idea is the varying of the electric current by varying the pressure between two points. Bell unquestionably suggested it in his famous patent, when he wrote of "increasing and diminishing the resistance." Berliner was the first actually to construct one. Edison greatly improved it by using soft carbon instead of a steel point. A Kentucky professor, David E. Hughes, started a new line of development by adapting a Bell telephone into a "microphone," a fantastic little instrument that would detect the noise made by a fly in walking across a table. Francis Blake, of Boston, changed a microphone into a practical transmitter. The Rev. Henry Hunnings, an English clergyman, hit upon the happy idea of using carbon in the form of small granules. And one of the Bell experts, named White, improved the Hunnings transmitter into its present shape. Both transmitter and receiver seem now to be as complete an artificial tongue and ear as human ingenuity can make them. They have persistently grown more elaborate, until today a telephone set, as it stands on a desk, contains as many as one hundred and thirty separate pieces, as well as a saltspoonful of glistening granules of carbon.

    继发射机之后，接下来便是神秘噪音的问题。这或许是所有电话问题中最怪异、最令人费解的一个。事实上，电话将一个奇妙的全新声音世界带到了人们的听觉范围之内。当时所有的电话线都是单根的，两端都接地，形成所谓的“接地电路”。而这种与大地（实际上是一个巨大的磁体）的连接，会在电话线上产生各种各样奇怪而刺耳的噪音。

    Next after the transmitter came the problem of the MYSTERIOUS NOISES. This was, perhaps, the most weird and mystifying of all the telephone problems. The fact was that the telephone had brought within hearing distance a new wonder- world of sound. All wires at that time were single, and ran into the earth at each end, making what was called a "grounded circuit." And this connection with the earth, which is really a big magnet, caused all manner of strange and uncouth noises on the telephone wires.

    噪音！如此嘈杂混乱的噪音，人类的耳朵从未听过。有喷溅声、气泡声，有抽搐声、嘶嘶声，有呼啸声和尖叫声。有树叶沙沙作响，青蛙呱呱叫，蒸汽嘶嘶作响，鸟儿拍打翅膀。有电报线的咔哒声，其他电话断断续续的通话声，还有一些奇怪的细小尖叫声，与任何已知的声音都截然不同。东西走向的线路比南北走向的线路噪音更大。夜晚比白天更嘈杂，在午夜时分，不知何故，这巴别塔般的噪音达到了顶峰。天马行空的沃森认为，这些声音或许是火星或其他某个宜居星球上的居民发出的信号。但务实的年轻电话员们一致认为，罪魁祸首是“感应”——一个含义模糊的词，通常指的是电的自然干扰。

    Noises! Such a jangle of meaningless noises had never been heard by human ears. There were spluttering and bubbling, jerking and rasping, whistling and screaming. There were the rustling of leaves, the croaking of frogs, the hissing of steam, and the flapping of birds' wings. There were clicks from telegraph wires, scraps of talk from other telephones, and curious little squeals that were unlike any known sound. The lines running east and west were noisier than the lines running north and south. The night was noisier than the day, and at the ghostly hour of midnight, for what strange reason no one knows, the babel was at its height. Watson, who had a fanciful mind, suggested that perhaps these sounds were signals from the inhabitants of Mars or some other sociable planet. But the matter- of-fact young telephonists agreed to lay the blame on "induction"--a hazy word which usually meant the natural meddlesomeness of electricity.

    无论那些神秘的噪音究竟是什么，它们都令人烦恼。可怜的电话公司几乎被折磨得快要崩溃了。它就像一条尾巴上拴着罐头的狗，无论走到哪里，都摆脱不了这怪异的噪音。“我们都不好意思去报账单，”最早的代理商之一A.A. Adee说道，“因为不管一个人对着电话说得多么清楚，电话那头的人听起来都像是在说乔克托语。”

    Whatever else the mysterious noises were, they were a nuisance. The poor little telephone business was plagued almost out of its senses. It was like a dog with a tin can tied to its tail. No matter where it went, it was pursued by this unearthly clatter. "We were ashamed to present our bills," said A. A. Adee, one of the first agents; "for no matter how plainly a man talked into his telephone, his language was apt to sound like Choctaw at the other end of the line."

    人们煞费苦心地尝试了各种方法来消除电线的噪音，但每一种方法通常都像念咒语一样徒劳无功。该怎么办呢？电话工人一步步被逼退。他们遭到殴打。这些噪音根本无法消除。他们无奈地同意，唯一的办法就是将每根电线的末端从污染的泥土中拔出，然后用另一根电线将它们连接起来。这就是所谓的“金属电路”。这意味着电线的使用量将大幅增加。这将迫使人们重建交换机，并发明新的信号系统。但这不可避免；1883年，当关于金属电路的争论正酣时，一位年轻人悄悄地在波士顿和普罗维登斯之间的一条新线路上应用了这种技术。效果神奇。“终于，”欣喜若狂的经理说，“我们拥有了一条完全安静的线路。”

    All manner of devices were solemnly tried to hush the wires, and each one usually proved to be as futile as an incantation. What was to be done? Step by step the telephone men were driven back.
