It is rather to make the telephone as universal as the water faucet, to bring within speaking distance every economic unit, to connect to the social organism every person who may at any time be needed. Just as the click of the reaper means bread, and the purr of the sewing-machine means clothes, and the roar of the Bessemer converter means steel, and the rattle of the press means education, so the ring of the telephone bell has come to mean unity and organization.

    如今，借助电缆、电报和电话，文明世界中任何两个城镇之间的距离都不会超过一小时。我们甚至能在十二分钟内将电报环绕地球。我们让纽约市的任何人只需二十一秒就能与任何其他纽约市民交谈。我们并不满足于建立这样一套交通系统，让我们能够随时随地从任何地方出发；我们也不满足于建立这样一套通讯系统，让新闻和八卦成为各国人民的共同财富。我们更进一步。我们在每个人口稠密的地区都建立了一套语音神经系统，让每个人都能与其他人直接通话，神奇地消除了距离的障碍，使美国变成了三千英里外的邻里，彼此紧挨着。

    Already, by cable, telegraph, and telephone, no two towns in the civilized world are more than one hour apart. We have even girdled the earth with a cablegram in twelve minutes. We have made it possible for any man in New York City to enter into conversation with any other New Yorker in twenty-one seconds. We have not been satisfied with establishing such a system of transportation that we can start any day for anywhere from anywhere else; neither have we been satisfied with establishing such a system of communication that news and gossip are the common property of all nations. We have gone farther. We have established in every large region of population a system of voice-nerves that puts every man at every other man's ear, and which so magically eliminates the factor of distance that the United States becomes three thousand miles of neighbors, side by side.

    这种征服时间和空间的努力，归根结底是物质进步的本能。缩短距离，延长时间——这一直是人类最主要的追求之一。因此，电话的更深层意义在于，它远不止是一种便利工具。它不能与安全剃须刀、钢琴家和钢笔相提并论。它是文明的高速工具，推动整个社会机制运转，从而提供更高效的社会服务。它是国家效率和合作的象征。

    This effort to conquer Time and Space is above all else the instinct of material progress. To shrivel up the miles and to stretch out the minutes--this has been one of the master passions of the human race. And thus the larger truth about the telephone is that it is vastly more than a mere convenience. It is not to be classed with safety razors and piano players and fountain pens. It is nothing less than the high-speed tool of civilization, gearing up the whole mechanism to more effective social service. It is the symbol of national efficiency and coperation.

    电话所做的一切，每年给国家造成的总成本可能高达2亿美元——这还不到美国农民十天的收入。我们为电话支付的价格，与土豆、三分之一的干草或八分之一的玉米的价格相同。每五美分的电费中，就有一美分用于电话。如果我们少喝一杯酒，少抽一支烟，就能付清电话费，还能剩下几百万美元。租用打字机、每天乘坐两次有轨电车或每天擦一次鞋的人，花同样的钱就能享受到非常好的电话服务。仅仅1910年纽约市政府铲除一场暴风雪的花费，就相当于五六年电话费的总和。

    All this the telephone is doing, at a total cost to the nation of probably $200,000,000 a year-- no more than American farmers earn in ten days. We pay the same price for it as we do for the potatoes, or for one-third of the hay crop, or for one-eighth of the corn. Out of every nickel spent for electrical service, one cent goes to the telephone. We could settle our telephone bill, and have several millions left over, if we cut off every fourth glass of liquor and smoke of tobacco. Whoever rents a typewriting machine, or uses a street car twice a day, or has his shoes polished once a day, may for the same expense have a very good telephone service. Merely to shovel away the snow of a single storm in 1910 cost the city government of New York as much as it will pay for five or six years of telephoning.

    电话的低廉程度令人难以置信，但这种低廉的程度至今仍远未被大众普遍认知，这主要是心理因素造成的。电话本身并不引人注目。它并不庞大，不像辛格大厦或卢西塔尼亚号那样气势恢宏。它的电线、交换机和电池散落在各处，隐藏在隐蔽之处，很少有人能够充分想象出它们错综复杂的全貌。试想一下，如果能把纽约一百多座电话大楼集中到一个巨大的广场上，如果两千名职员、三千名维修工和六千名女接线员每天早上都伴着乐队和旗帜列队上班，那么，或许就能营造出那种任何伟大理念都必须具备的震撼力，从而深入人心。

    This almost incredible cheapness of telephony is still far from being generally perceived, mainly for psychological reasons. A telephone is not impressive. It has no bulk. It is not like the Singer Building or the Lusitania. Its wires and switchboards and batteries are scattered and hidden, and few have sufficient imagination to picture them in all their complexity. If only it were possible to assemble the hundred or more telephone buildings of New York in one vast plaza, and if the two thousand clerks and three thousand maintenance men and six thousand girl operators were to march to work each morning with bands and banners, then, perhaps, there might be the necessary quality of impressiveness by which any large idea must always be imparted to the public mind.

    由于缺少七美分半的硬币，如今即使在美国最大的城市，五美分的电话服务也已普及。只需五美分，任何人都可以享受一整套线路系统，这套系统日夜运转，随时待命。这套系统可能耗资两千万到五千万美元，但租用它的费用却只有租一辆汽车的八分之一。即使是长途电话，与往返火车票的价格相比，通话费用也显得微不足道。例如，从纽约到费城的通话费用为七十五美分，而火车票价则为四美元。从纽约到芝加哥的通话费用为五美元，而火车票价则为七十美元。正如哈里曼曾经说过的那样：“我连从家到车站的路费都比不上打一次奥马哈电话的钱。”

    For lack of a seven and one-half cent coin, there is now five-cent telephony even in the largest American cities. For five cents whoever wishes has an entire wire-system at his service, a system that is kept waiting by day and night, so that it will be ready the instant he needs it. This system may have cost from twenty to fifty millions, yet it may be hired for one-eighth the cost of renting an automobile. Even in long- distance telephony, the expense of a message dwindles when it is compared with the price of a return railway ticket. A talk from New York to Philadelphia, for instance, costs seventy-five cents, while the railway fare would be four dollars. From New York to Chicago a talk costs five dollars as against seventy dollars by rail. As Harriman once said, "I can't get from my home to the depot for the price of a talk to Omaha."

    要说所有投资电话的人的净利润是多少，始终只能靠猜测。人们普遍认为贝尔公司的股票持有者一夜暴富，这种说法是夸大其词，是那些投机取巧的公司的发起人不断渲染的结果。事实上，根本没有人因此发了财。“我不相信，”西奥多·韦尔说，“有人靠电话赚到了一百万美元。” 那些不发行掺水股票、不将特许经营权资本化的公司，不太可能有人一夜暴富。相反，直到1897年，贝尔公司的股东支付的金额比面值多出了470万美元；而在尤宁·N·贝瑟尔担任总裁期间，最近东部地区的公司合并后，新发行的股票实际上比注销的股票少了800万美元。

    To say what the net profits have been, to the entire body of people who have invested money in the telephone, will always be more or less of a guess. The general belief that immense fortunes were made by the lucky holders of Bell stock, is an exaggeration that has been kept alive by the promoters of wildcat companies. No such fortunes were made. "I do not believe," says Theodore Vail, "that any one man ever made a clear million out of the telephone." There are not apt to be any get-rich-quick for- tunes made in corporations that issue no watered stock and do not capitalize their franchises. On the contrary, up to 1897, the holders of stock in the Bell Companies had paid in four million, seven hundred thousand dollars more than the par value; and in the recent consolidation of Eastern companies, under the presidency of Union N. Bethell, the new stock was actually eight millions less than the stock that was retired.

    起初，很少有电话公司盈利。他们低估了建设和维护成本。丹佛预计成本为2500美元，结果却花了6万美元。布法罗预计支付3000美元，结果却不得不支付15万美元。此外，他们还意外地发现，由于通话量更大，200户的交换机成本是100户交换机的两倍多。通常，支付给电话公司的每一美元都按以下方式分配：

    Few telephone companies paid any profits at first. They had undervalued the cost of building and maintenance. Denver expected the cost to be two thousand, five hundred dollars and spent sixty thousand dollars. Buffalo expected to pay three thousand dollars and had to pay one hundred and fifty thousand dollars. Also, they made the unwelcome discovery that an exchange of two hundred costs more than twice as much as an exchange of one hundred, because of the greater amount of traffic. Usually a dollar that is paid to a telephone company is divided as follows:

    租金............ 4美分 税金............ 4美分 利息............ 6美分 盈余............ 8美分 维护费............ 16美分 股息............ 18美分 人工费............ 44美分 ---- 1.00美元

    Rent ............ 4c Taxes ........... 4c Interest ........ 6c Surplus ......... 8c Maintenance .... 16c Dividends ...... 18c Labor .......... 44c ---- $1.00

    大多数费率问题（此类问题不胜枚举）的出现，都是因为人们对电话业务缺乏了解。事实上，直到最近，电话业务本身也缺乏了解。它一直坚持地方化和个体化的经营理念，迟迟不愿在不盈利的地方安装电话，并期望每台电话都能盈利。在许多州，电话公司和公众都忽略了最关键的一点：电话系统的各个成员首先是相互依存的。

    Most of the rate troubles (and their name has been legion) have arisen because the telephone business was not understood. In fact, until recently, it did not understand itself. It persisted in holding to a local and individualistic view of its business. It was slow to put telephones in unprofitable places. It expected every instrument to pay its way. In many States, both the telephone men and the public overlooked the most vital fact in the case, which is that the members of a telephone system are above all else INTERDEPENDENT.

    一部电话本身毫无价值。它就像从管风琴上切下来的簧片或从手上砍下的手指一样毫无用处。它既不美观，也无法用于其他任何用途。它完全不同于钢琴或留声机，后者拥有独立的存在。电话的价值取决于它能接入多少其他电话。而且，任何地方的每一部电话都会为同一线路系统上的其他所有电话增添价值。简而言之，这就是公平费率的关键所在。

    One telephone by itself has no value. It is as useless as a reed cut out of an organ or a finger that is severed from a hand. It is not even ornamental or adaptable to any other pur- pose. It is not at all like a piano or a talking- machine, which has a separate existence. It is useful only in proportion to the number of other telephones it reaches. AND EVERY TELEPHONE ANYWHERE ADDS VALUE TO EVERY OTHER TELEPHONE ON THE SAME SYSTEM OF WIRES. That, in a sentence, is the keynote of equitable rates.

    为了公共利益，许多电话必须安装在那些并非主要用途的地方。因为在任何时候都可能出现突发紧急情况，使电话在那一刻变得至关重要。尤其是在汽车普及之后，几乎每个角落都可能时不时地需要发送信息。宾夕法尼亚铁路公司最近就以非常实际的方式践行了这一原则，该公司自费在其位于阿尔图纳的工人家中安装了525部电话。同样，电话公司显然也有责任扩大其网络覆盖范围，直至覆盖所有地点，然后尽可能公平地分配其总费用。所有费用必须由所有用户承担——这才是立法机构和电话公司最终都必须认可的收费理念。当然，它永远无法被简化为一套固定的体系或公式。它始终是一个需要协商和妥协的问题，需要高超的技巧和极大的耐心。但是，一旦理解了其基本原则，就不会出现什么严重的问题了。

    Many a telephone, for the general good, must be put where it does not earn its own living. At any time some sudden emergency may arise that will make it for the moment priceless. Especially since the advent of the automobile, there is no nook or corner from which it may not be supremely necessary, now and then, to send a message. This principle was acted upon recently in a most practical way by the Pennsylvania Railroad, which at its own expense installed five hundred and twenty-five telephones in the homes of its workmen in Altoona. In the same way, it is clearly the social duty of the telephone company to widen out its system until every point is covered, and then to distribute its gross charges as fairly as it can. The whole must carry the whole--that is the philosophy of rates which must finally be recognized by legislatures and telephone companies alike. It can never, of course, be reduced to a system or formula. It will always be a matter of opinion and compromise, requiring much skill and much patience. But there will seldom be any serious trouble when once its basic principles are understood.

    就像所有节省时间的发明一样，比如铁路、收割机和贝塞麦转炉，归根结底，电话本身并不需要成本；真正需要成本的是缺乏电话。最强大的国家往往是没有电话的国家。

    Like all time-saving inventions, like the railroad, the reaper, and the Bessemer converter, the telephone, in the last analysis, COSTS NOTHING; IT IS THE LACK OF IT THAT COSTS. THE NATION THAT MOST IS THE NATION WITHOUT IT.

    第八章 外国的电话

    CHAPTER VIII. THE TELEPHONE IN FOREIGN COUNTRIES

    电话问世近一年后，欧洲才开始注意到它的存在。直到1877年3月3日，《伦敦雅典娜神庙》杂志才用寥寥数语提及了电话，它才引起公众的关注。除了那些想找点乐子的人之外，电话并不受欢迎。对整个商业界而言，在四五年的时间里，它就像一个科学界的“比尔肯”（Billiken，一种虚构的玩意儿），对严肃的人们来说，它永远也派不上用场。

    The telephone was nearly a year old before Europe was aware of its existence. It received no public notice of any kind whatever until March 3, 1877, when the London Athenaeum mentioned it in a few careful sentences. It was not welcomed, except by those who wished an evening's entertainment. And to the entire commercial world it was for four or five years a sort of scientific Billiken, that never could be of any service to serious people.

    一批又一批的美国热心人士怀揣着欧洲各国渴望普及电话系统的梦想，匆匆赶往欧洲，却一个接一个地失败了。弗雷德里克·A·高尔是其中的第一位。他是一位富有冒险精神的商业奇才，为了成为一名四处奔走的宣传员，他放弃了代理商的合同。后来，他遇到了一位歌剧女主角，与她坠入爱河并结为夫妻，放弃了电话事业，转而投身热气球飞行，最终在试图飞越英吉利海峡时不幸丧生。

    One after another, several American enthusiasts rushed posthaste to Europe, with dreams of eager nations clamoring for telephone systems, and one after another they failed. Frederick A. Gower was the first of these. He was an adventurous chevalier of business who gave up an agent's contract in return for a right to become a roving propagandist. Later he met a prima donna, fell in love with and married her, forsook telephony for ballooning, and lost his life in attempting to fly across the English Channel.

    接下来是来自普罗维登斯的威廉·H·雷诺兹，他以五千美元的价格买下了英国专利的五分之八，又以两千五百美元的价格买下了俄罗斯、西班牙、葡萄牙和意大利专利权的一半。从他保存至今的一封信中，我们可以了解他当时的处境。“我在伦敦工作了四个月，”他写道，“我去过英格兰银行和其他地方；但我找不到一个愿意为电话投一先令的人。”

    Next went William H. Reynolds, of Providence, who had bought five-eights of the British patent for five thousand dollars, and half the right to Russia, Spain, Portugal, and Italy for two thousand, five hundred dollars. How he was received may be seen from a letter of his which has been preserved. "I have been working in London for four months," he writes; "I have been to the Bank of England and elsewhere; and I have not found one man who will put one shilling into the telephone."

    1878年，贝尔在蜜月旅行期间匆匆前往英国和苏格兰，满怀希望地期待自己的发明能在故乡得到认可。然而，从商业角度来看，他的这次旅行彻底失败了。他收到了无数的宴请，却没有拿到任何合同；最终，他带着贫困和沮丧的心情回到了美国。随后，乐观的贝尔的岳父加德纳·G·哈伯德（Gardiner G. Hubbard）逆势而上，组建了国际电话公司和东方电话公司，但最终也一无所获。同年，就连精明的西方电气公司创始人伊诺斯·M·巴顿（Enos M. Barton）也前往法国和英国，试图开拓电话出口贸易，结果同样以失败告终。

    Bell himself hurried to England and Scotland on his wedding tour in 1878, with great expectations of having his invention appreciated in his native land. But from a business point of view, his mission was a total failure. He received dinners a-plenty, but no contracts; and came back to the United States an impoverished and disheartened man. Then the optimistic Gardiner G. Hubbard, Bell's father-in-law, threw himself against the European inertia and organized the International and Oriental Telephone Companies, which came to nothing of any importance. In the same year even Enos M. Barton, the sagacious founder of the Western Electric, went to France and England to establish an export trade in telephones, and failed.

    这些才华横溢的人发现，他们的计划因公众的冷漠，甚至公开的敌意而受挫。《星期六评论》评论道：“电话不过是个玩具，它或许能让无知的人一时惊叹，但它远不如成熟的空气管系统。”另一位伦敦编辑问道：“人们的隐私将何去何从？家庭的宁静又将何去何从？”作家们竞相想方设法嘲讽贝尔及其发明。“它简直太简单了，”一位作家说道。“它不过是个电动的传声筒，”另一位作家说道。“它不过是个复杂的喇叭，”第三位作家说道。起初，除了潜水员和煤矿工人，没有一位英国编辑能想到电话的任何用途。价格也引起了普遍的抗议。街头巷尾充斥着大量玩具电话，每个售价仅为一先令。尽管政府每年收取六十美元的电报印刷费用，但人们对电话收费却只有电报印刷费用的一半，强烈抗议。直到1882年，赫伯特·斯宾塞仍然写道：“电话在伦敦几乎无人使用，在英国其他城市更是闻所未闻。”

    These able men found their plans thwarted by the indifference of the public, and often by open hostility. "The telephone is little better than a toy," said the Saturday Review; "it amazes ignorant people for a moment, but it is inferior to the well-established system of air- tubes." "What will become of the privacy of life?" asked another London editor. "What will become of the sanctity of the domestic hearth?" Writers vied with each other in inventing methods of pooh-poohing Bell and his invention. "It is ridiculously simple," said one. "It is only an electrical speaking-tube," said another. "It is a complicated form of speaking- trumpet," said a third. No British editor could at first conceive of any use for the telephone, except for divers and coal miners. The price, too, created a general outcry. Floods of toy telephones were being sold on the streets at a shilling apiece; and although the Government was charging sixty dollars a year for the use of its printing-telegraphs, people protested loudly against paying half as much for telephones. As late as 1882, Herbert Spencer writes: "The telephone is scarcely used at all in London, and is unknown in the other English cities."

    第一个真正与电话结缘的重要人物是开尔文勋爵，当时他还是个名不见经传的年轻科学家。他在费城百年庆典上见过最初的电话，并被其深深吸引，以至于冲动的贝尔先生竟将电话作为礼物送给了他。在下一次英国科学促进协会的会议上，开尔文勋爵展示了这些电话。他不仅如此，还成为了电话的拥护者，甚至不惜以自己的声誉担保电话的合法性。他讲述了在百年庆典上进行的测试，并向持怀疑态度的科学家们保证，他并没有被欺骗。“所有这一切都是我亲耳听到的，”他说，“这块圆形的铁盘清晰无误地告诉我的。”

    The first man of consequence to befriend the telephone was Lord Kelvin, then an untitled young scientist. He had seen the original telephones at the Centennial in Philadelphia, and was so fascinated with them that the impulsive Bell had thrust them into his hands as a gift. At the next meeting of the British Association for the Advancement of Science, Lord Kelvin exhibited these. He did more. He became the champion of the telephone. He staked his reputation upon it. He told the story of the tests made at the Centennial, and assured the sceptical scientists that he had not been deceived. "All this my own ears heard," he said, "spoken to me with unmistakable distinctness by this circular disc of iron."

    科学家和电气专家们大多分成了两派。一些人认为电话是不可能的，而另一些人则说“再简单不过了”。几乎所有人都认为贝尔的发明不过是件滑稽的小事。但开尔文勋爵坚持己见。他反复强调，电话是“科学史上最有趣的发明之一”。他甚至在煤矿里用电话线的一端进行了演示。在格拉斯哥的一次公开会议上，他与贝尔并肩而立，并宣布：

    The scientists and electrical experts were, for the most part, split up into two camps. Some of them said the telephone was impossible, while others said that "nothing could be simpler." Almost all were agreed that what Bell had done was a humorous trifle. But Lord Kelvin persisted. He hammered the truth home that the telephone was "one of the most interesting inventions that has ever been made in the history of science." He gave a demonstration with one end of the wire in a coal mine. He stood side by side with Bell at a public meeting in Glasgow, and declared:

    “贝尔之前的那些被称为电话的东西，与贝尔的电话截然不同，就像一连串的拍手声与人声截然不同一样。它们实际上是电击产生的拍手声；而贝尔构思了——完全原创和新颖的想法——使电击持续不断，从而完美地再现人声。”

    "The things that were called telephones before Bell were as different from Bell's telephone as a series of hand-claps are different from the human voice. They were in fact electrical claps; while Bell conceived the idea--THE WHOLLY ORIGINAL AND NOVEL IDEA--of giving continuity to the shocks, so as to perfectly reproduce the human voice."

    科学家们不得不一个接一个地认真对待电话。在一次公开测试中，一位著名的教授仍然持怀疑态度。他被要求发送一条信息。他带着难以置信的笑容走到电话前，以为整个演示是个玩笑，便对着话筒喊道：“嗨，滴滴滴——跟上来。”然后他听着回应。他脸上的表情瞬间变成了无比惊讶。“上面写着——‘猫和提琴’，”他倒吸一口凉气，立刻就成了电话的拥趸。通过这样的测试，科学家们逐渐被说服，到了1877年中期，贝尔在普利茅斯举行的科学年会上发表讲话时，受到了“热烈的欢迎”。

    One by one the scientists were forced to take the telephone seriously. At a public test there was one noted professor who still stood in the ranks of the doubters. He was asked to send a message. He went to the instrument with a grin of incredulity, and thinking the whole exhibition a joke, shouted into the mouthpiece: "Hi diddle diddle--follow up that." Then he listened for an answer. The look on his face changed to one of the utmost amazement. "It says--`The cat and the fiddle,'" he gasped, and forthwith he became a convert to telephony. By such tests the men of science were won over, and by the middle of 1877 Bell received a "vociferous welcome" when he addressed them at their annual convention at Plymouth.

    不久之后，《伦敦时报》也投降了。它来了个180度大转弯，对电话大加赞扬。“突然之间，悄无声息地，全人类都被拉到了可以说话和听的距离之内，”它惊呼道，“几乎没有什么比这更令人渴望，也更不可能实现的了。”下一个退出嘲讽行列的是《闲谈者》杂志，它在社论结尾写道：“我们不禁被这幅画面所震撼：一个孩子竟然能驾驭自然界最微妙、最强大的力量，像奴隶一样将一些低语传递到世界各地。”

    Soon afterwards, The London Times surrendered. It whirled right-about-face and praised the telephone to the skies. "Suddenly and quietly the whole human race is brought within speaking and hearing distance," it exclaimed; "scarcely anything was more desired and more impossible." The next paper to quit the mob of scoffers was the Tatler, which said in an editorial peroration, "We cannot but feel im- pressed by the picture of a human child commanding the subtlest and strongest force in Nature to carry, like a slave, some whisper around the world."

    紧随科学家和编辑之后的是贵族们。凯斯内斯伯爵率先登场。他公开宣称：“电话是我一生中见过的最不可思议的东西。”1878年一个冬日的清晨，维多利亚女王驱车前往伦敦托马斯·比德尔夫爵士的府邸，与坐在唐宁街办公室的凯特·菲尔德通了一个小时的电话。菲尔德小姐演唱了《凯瑟琳·莫沃琳》，女王在电话中向她表示感谢，并说她“非常高兴”。女王向在场的贝尔先生表示祝贺，并询问是否可以购买这两部电话；贝尔先生随即赠予她一对象牙电话。

    Closely after the scientists and editors came the nobility. The Earl of Caithness led the way. He declared in public that "the telephone is the most extraordinary thing I ever saw in my life." And one wintry morning in 1878 Queen Victoria drove to the house of Sir Thomas Biddulph, in London, and for an hour talked and listened by telephone to Kate Field, who sat in a Downing Street office. Miss Field sang "Kathleen Mavourneen," and the Queen thanked her by telephone, saying she was "immensely pleased." She congratulated Bell himself, who was present, and asked if she might be permitted to buy the two telephones; whereupon Bell presented her with a pair done in ivory.

    不难想象，这件事极大地提升了英国电话的声誉。温莎城堡立刻架设了一条电线。《每日新闻》、波斯大使以及五六位贵族和男爵也纷纷订购了电线。随后，摩根银行的一份订单更是让电话从业者们欣喜若狂。这是商界和金融界“权贵”首次对电话表示认可。伦敦迅速开通了一个小型交换机，配备了十条电线；1879年4月2日，贝尔公司年轻的经理西奥多·韦尔向波士顿的工厂下达命令：“请尽快生产一百部用于出口的手持电话。” 海外贸易由此拉开帷幕。

    This incident, as may be imagined, did much to establish the reputation of telephony in Great Britain. A wire was at once strung to Windsor Castle. Others were ordered by the Daily News, the Persian Ambassador, and five or six lords and baronets. Then came an order which raised the hopes of the telephone men to the highest heaven, from the banking house of J. S. Morgan Co. It was the first recognition from the "seats of the mighty" in the business and financial world. A tiny exchange, with ten wires, was promptly started in London; and on April 2d, 1879, Theodore Vail, the young manager of the Bell Company, sent an order to the factory in Boston, "Please make one hundred hand telephones for export trade as early as possible." The foreign trade had begun.

    随后，晴天霹雳，一场完全出乎意料的灾难降临。正当几家充满活力的公司如雨后春笋般涌现之际，邮政总局局长突然宣布电话属于电报的一种。根据英国法律，电报必须是政府垄断的。这项法律在电话诞生六年前就已通过，但这无关紧要。电话公司员工抗议并据理力争。廷德尔和开尔文勋爵警告政府，他们犯了一个无法辩解的错误。但一切都已成定局。正如最初的铁路被称为收费公路一样，电话也被郑重宣布为电报。更荒诞的是，高等法院的斯蒂芬法官最终裁定电话在法律上属于电报，并引用了韦氏词典中的一段话来支持他的观点——而韦氏词典的出版时间比电话发明早了二十年。

    Then there came a thunderbolt out of a blue sky, a wholly unforeseen disaster. Just as a few energetic companies were sprouting up, the Postmaster General suddenly proclaimed that the telephone was a species of telegraph. According to a British law the telegraph was required to be a Government monopoly. This law had been passed six years before the telephone was born, but no matter. The telephone men protested and argued. Tyndall and Lord Kelvin warned the Government that it was making an indefensible mistake. But nothing could be done. Just as the first railways had been called toll-roads, so the telephone was solemnly declared to be a telegraph. Also, to add to the absurd humor of the situation, Judge Stephen, of the High Court of Justice, spoke the final word that compelled the telephone legally to be a telegraph, and sustained his opinion by a quotation from Webster's Dictionary, which was published twenty years before the telephone was invented.

    抓住了这个新对手之后，下一步该怎么办？邮政总局局长一筹莫展。他当然对电话业务一窍不通，电报部门的官员们也一样。既没有书籍可以参考，也没有学院可以指导他。当时的电报业务和今天一样，都是失败的生意，根本无法维持运营。因此，他不敢承担建设第二套线路系统的风险，最终只好同意向私营公司发放许可证。

    Having captured this new rival, what next? The Postmaster General did not know. He had, of course, no experience in telephony, and neither had any of his officials in the telegraph department. There was no book and no college to instruct him. His telegraph was then, as it is to-day, a business failure. It was not earning its keep. Therefore he did not dare to shoulder the risk of constructing a second system of wires, and at last consented to give licenses to private companies.

    但混乱仍在继续。为了促进竞争，根据当时的学术理论，邮政部门向十三家私营公司发放了许可证。不出所料，实力最强的公司很快就吞并了其他十二家。如果放任不管，这家公司或许能提供优质的服务，但它却被繁琐的规章制度束缚，举步维艰。它被迫将总收入的十分之一上缴邮政局，并被要求在六个月内做好出售的准备。而且，就在它架设好长途线路系统后，邮政总局局长立即出手将其收回。

    But the muddle continued. In order to compel competition, according to the academic theories of the day, licenses were given to thir- teen private companies. As might have been expected, the ablest company quickly swallowed the other twelve. If it had been let alone, this company might have given good service, but it was hobbled and fenced in by jealous regulations. It was compelled to pay one-tenth of its gross earnings to the Post Office. It was to hold itself ready to sell out at six months' notice. And as soon as it had strung a long-distance system of wires, the Postmaster General pounced down upon it and took it away.

    1900年，邮政总局抛弃了对特许经营公司的所有义务，放任自由竞争。它着手在伦敦建立第二套电话系统，两年后才发现自己犯了错误，并提出合作。邮政总局向五个要求市政所有制的城市发放了许可证。这些城市鼓声震天，雄心勃勃地开始了这项事业，却接连遭遇各种挫折，最终放弃。就连市政所有制的先驱城市格拉斯哥，也在电话领域遭遇了滑铁卢。它斥资180万美元购置了一套当时就已经过时的设备，亏损运营了一段时间后，于1906年以152.5万美元的价格将其卖给了邮政总局。

    Then, in 1900, the Post Office tossed aside all obligations to the licensed company, and threw open the door to a free-for-all competition. It undertook to start a second system in London, and in two years discovered its blunder and proposed to cooperate. It granted licenses to five cities that demanded municipal ownership. These cities set out bravely, with loud beating of drums, plunged from one mishap to another, and finally quit. Even Glasgow, the premier city of municipal ownership, met its Waterloo in the telephone. It spent one million, eight hundred thousand dollars on a plant that was obsolete when it was new, ran it for a time at a loss, and then sold it to the Post Office in 1906 for one million, five hundred and twenty-five thousand dollars.

    因此，从始至终，英国电话的发展史堪称一出“闹剧”。如今，英国和爱尔兰岛上共有不到六十万部电话在使用。伦敦占地六百四十平方英里，拥有其中的四分之一，并且每年还在以一万部的速度增长。由于邮政局已宣布将于1912年元旦接管所有私营电话公司，因此目前并无大规模的改进措施。看来，这种官僚主义的混乱局面将会无限期地持续下去。

    So, from first to last, the story of the telephone in Great Britain has been a "comedy of errors." There are now, in the two islands, not six hundred thousand telephones in use. London, with its six hundred and forty square miles of houses, has one-quarter of these, and is gaining at the rate of ten thousand a year. No large improvements are under way, as the Post Office has given notice that it will take over and operate all private companies on New Year's Day, 1912. The bureaucratic muddle, so it seems, is to continue indefinitely.

    德国也面临着同样的官僚主义负担，但支持力度和资源投入却相对较少。德国实行完全的政府垄断。任何人如果将电话​​服务出租给邻居，都可能被判处六个月监禁。邮政总局局长在这里也拥有至高无上的权力。他将电话业务强行纳入邮政体系。小城市的居民必须支付与大城市居民支付的同等费用才能享受小型服务。德国的电话服务效率尚可，但速度并不快，也未打破任何纪录。德国工程师并没有密切关注美国电话技术的发展。他们更倾向于自行研发方法，因此创造出了各种各样的系统，有好有坏，也有平庸之作。总而言之，德国的电话系统投资可能高达七千五百万美元，总共安装了九十万部电话。

    In Germany there has been the same burden of bureaucracy, but less backing and filling. There is a complete government monopoly. Whoever commits the crime of leasing telephone service to his neighbors may be sent to jail for six months. Here, too, the Postmaster General has been supreme. He has forced the telephone business into a postal mould. The man in a small city must pay as high a rate for a small service, as the man in a large city pays for a large service. There is a fair degree of efficiency, but no high speed or record-breaking. The German engineers have not kept in close touch with the progress of telephony in the United States. They have preferred to devise methods of their own, and so have created a miscellaneous assortment of systems, good, bad, and indifferent. All told, there is probably an investment of seventy-five million dollars and a total of nine hundred thousand telephones.

    电话一直深受德皇的喜爱。他有个习惯，每次计划狩猎时，都会让人架设一条特殊的电线连接到森林总部，以便每天早上与内阁成员通话。他还通过电话授予学位和荣誉。就连他的前任首相冯·比洛也是通过这种非正式的方式获得了伯爵头衔。但德国第一个真正热爱电话的人是俾斯麦。这位昔日的统一者立刻意识到电话在维系国家团结方面的价值，并下令在柏林的宫殿和位于瓦尔津的农场之间架设一条电话线，两地相距230英里。这早在1877年秋季就已完成，因此也是欧洲第一条长途电话线。

    Telephony has always been in high favor with the Kaiser. It is his custom, when planning a hunting party, to have a special wire strung to the forest headquarters, so that he can converse every morning with his Cabinet. He has conferred degrees and honors by telephone. Even his former Chancellor, Von Buelow, received his title of Count in this informal way. But the first friend of the telephone in Germany was Bismarck. The old Unifier saw instantly its value in holding a nation together, and ordered a line between his palace in Berlin and his farm at Varzin, which lay two hundred and thirty miles apart. This was as early as the Fall of 1877, and was thus the first long-distance line in Europe.

    在法国，如同在英国一样，政府在私人公民完成电话业务的先驱工作后不久便迅速接管了这项业务。1889年，政府实际上没收了巴黎的电话系统，并在经过九年的诉讼后向其所有者支付了五百万法郎。这种鲁莽的开端使法国的电话系统每况愈下。它不仅汇集了其他国家的所有错误，还创造了许多自己的错误。几乎所有已知的官僚主义弊端都被发挥了出来。收费制度被彻底颠覆；原本只适用于小城市的固定费率被推广到大城市，而原本只适用于大城市的电报费率也被推广到小城镇。女接线员们被困在错综复杂的公务员制度中。她们未经邮政总局局长的许可不得结婚；而且无论如何都不能嫁给市长、警察、出纳员或外国人，以免泄露电话交换机的秘密。

    In France, as in England, the Government seized upon the telephone business as soon as the pioneer work had been done by private citizens. In 1889 it practically confiscated the Paris system, and after nine years of litigation paid five million francs to its owners. With this reckless beginning, it floundered from bad to worse. It assembled the most complete assortment of other nations' mistakes, and invented several of its own. Almost every known evil of bureaucracy was developed. The system of rates was turned upside down; the flat rate, which can be profitably permitted in small cities only, was put in force in the large cities, and the message rate, which is applicable only to large cities, was put in force in small places. The girl operators were entangled in a maze of civil service rules. They were not allowed to marry without the permission of the Postmaster General; and on no account might they dare to marry a mayor, a policeman, a cashier, or a foreigner, lest they betray the secrets of the switchboard.

    当时既没有全国统一的计划，也没有标准化的规范，更没有发明家和改进人员。每个用户都必须自己购买电话。正如乔治·阿德所说：“在巴黎，任何挂在墙上的东西都可能是电话。” 因此，由于设备简陋和繁文缛节，法国的电话系统最终沦为如今电话领域最反面教材的典型案例。

    There was no national plan, no standardization, no staff of inventors and improvers. Every user was required to buy his own telephone. As George Ade has said, "Anything attached to a wall is liable to be a telephone in Paris." And so, what with poor equipment and red tape, the French system became what it remains to-day, the most conspicuous example of what NOT to do in telephony.

    整个法国的电话数量甚至还不及巴黎市应有的数量，甚至比不上现在芝加哥的电话数量。忍无可忍的巴黎市民已经发起抗议，他们提交了一份有三万两千人签名的请愿书，甚至还组织了一个“抗议者联盟”（Kickers' League）——这是世界上独一无二的组织——要求以合理的价格享受优质的电话服务。官僚主义的电话系统造成的每日损失已经非常巨大。“1907年电话恐慌那天，一个电话交换机里的笨手笨脚的女孩就让我损失了五千美元，”乔治·凯斯勒说道。然而，政府每年却从其电话垄断业务中净赚三百万美元；直到1910年成立了改善委员会之前，政府对公众的不便漠不关心。

    There are barely as many telephones in the whole of France as ought normally to be in the city of Paris. There are not as many as are now in use in Chicago. The exasperated Parisians have protested. They have presented a petition with thirty-two thousand names. They have even organized a "Kickers' League"--the only body of its kind in any country--to demand good service at a fair price. The daily loss from bureaucratic telephony has become enormous. "One blundering girl in a telephone exchange cost me five thousand dollars on the day of the panic in 1907," said George Kessler. But the Government clears a net profit of three million dollars a year from its telephone monopoly; and until 1910, when a committee of betterment was appointed, it showed no concern at the discomfort of the public.

    1908年，巴黎的电话总交换机被大火彻底烧毁，巴黎也因此深刻体会到了电话效率的重要性。“建造一个新的交换机，”欧洲的制造商们说，“需要四到五个月的时间。”这时，一位来自芝加哥的年轻人出现了。“我们可以在六十天内安装好一个新的交换机，”他说，“如果延误，我们每天罚款六百美元。”如此高效的工作效率前所未闻。但这正是芝加哥展现自身实力的机会。巴黎和芝加哥相距四千五百英里，需要十二天的车程。新的交换机长达一百八十英尺，由一万根电线组成。然而，西电公司仅用了三周时间就完成了这项工作。交换机被紧急装入六节货车车厢运往纽约，然后装上法国轮船“普罗旺斯号”，三十六天后运抵巴黎；因此，当六十天期限到来时，交换机已经投入使用，并配备了九十名接线员。

    There was one striking lesson in telephone efficiency which Paris received in 1908, when its main exchange was totally destroyed by fire. "To build a new switchboard," said European manufacturers, "will require four or five months." A hustling young Chicagoan appeared on the scene. "We 'll put in a new switchboard in sixty days," he said; "and agree to forfeit six hundred dollars a day for delay." Such quick work had never been known. But it was Chicago's chance to show what she could do. Paris and Chicago are four thousand, five hundred miles apart, a twelve days' journey. The switchboard was to be a hundred and eighty feet in length, with ten thousand wires. Yet the Western Electric finished it in three weeks. It was rushed on six freight-cars to New York, loaded on the French steamer La Provence, and deposited at Paris in thirty-six days; so that by the time the sixty days had expired, it was running full speed with a staff of ninety operators.

    俄罗斯和奥匈帝国目前各自拥有约12.5万部电话。两国在电话发展竞赛中并驾齐驱，而这场竞赛从来都不是一场快速的较量。两国政府都对电话行业疏于扶持，资金匮乏，发展缓慢，也从未采取任何措施来扩大电话业务。除了维也纳、布达佩斯、圣彼得堡和莫斯科之外，其他国家几乎没有像样的有线电话系统。奥匈帝国之间的政治僵局使得两国电话行业短期内难以迎来转机；但俄罗斯最近的政策变化或许会开启一个新时代。现在，每个城市都允许一家私营公司获得电话运营许可证，条件是该公司需缴纳3%的收入分成。这一举措使俄罗斯出人意料地跃居前列，如今，在电话从业者眼中，俄罗斯已成为欧洲最自由的国家。

    Russia and Austria-Hungary have now about one hundred and twenty-five thousand telephones apiece. They are neck and neck in a race that has not at any time been a fast one. In each country the Government has been a neglectful stepmother to the telephone. It has starved the business with a lack of capital and used no enterprise in expanding it. Outside of Vienna, Budapest, St. Petersburg, and Moscow there are no wire-systems of any consequence. The political deadlock between Austria and Hungary shuts out any immediate hope of a happier life for the telephone in those countries; but in Russia there has recently been a change in policy that may open up a new era. Permits are now being offered to one private company in each city, in return for three per cent of the revenue. By this step Russia has unexpectedly swept to the front and is now, to telephone men, the freest country in Europe.

    在瑞士这个小国，电话行业从一开始就由政府所有，但对企业的影响却比其他地方小得多。这里的官员们甚至放弃了电报，转而发展电话。他们看到了电话线对于维系山谷村庄的重要性；于是，他们用一套廉价而略显简陋的电话系统横跨阿尔卑斯山，每年承载着六千万次通话。就连负责营救被困雪中的旅行者的圣伯纳德修道院的僧侣们，如今也在山上安装了一系列电话亭。

    In tiny Switzerland there has been government ownership from the first, but with less detriment to the business than elsewhere. Here the officials have actually jilted the telegraph for the telephone. They have seen the value of the talking wire to hold their valley villages together; and so have cries-crossed the Alps with a cheap and somewhat flimsy system of telephony that carries sixty million conversations a year. Even the monks of St. Bernard, who rescue snowbound travellers, have now equipped their mountain with a series of telephone booths.

    世界上最高的电话位于意大利阿尔卑斯山的罗莎峰顶，海拔近三英里。它连接着一条通往罗马的线路，以便女王可以与一位教授通话。这位女王是意大利的玛格丽特公主，教授是天文学家莫索先生，他在罗莎峰上的天文台研究星空。女王自费雇佣了一队线路工人架设这条线路，他们在山上历经六年艰辛，最终才将其固定到位。意大利的整体情况与英国类似。政府一直垄断着长途电话线路，现在正准备收购所有私营公司。三千二百万人口只有五万五千部电话——与挪威持平，比丹麦少。在意大利南部和西西里岛的许多省份，电话铃声仍然很陌生。

    The highest telephone in the world is on the peak of Monte Rosa, in the Italian Alps, very nearly three miles above the level of the sea. It is linked to a line that runs to Rome, in order that a queen may talk to a professor. In this case the Queen is Margherita of Italy and the professor is Signor Mosso, the astronomer, who studies the heavens from an observatory on Monte Rosa. At her own expense, the Queen had this wire strung by a crew of linemen, who slipped and floundered on the mountain for six years before they had it pegged in place. The general situation in Italy is like that in Great Britain. The Government has always monop- olized the long-distance lines, and is now about to buy out all private companies. There are only fifty-five thousand telephones to thirty-two million people--as many as in Norway and less than in Denmark. And in many of the southern and Sicilian provinces the jingle of the telephone bell is still an unfamiliar sound.

    荷兰最大的特点在于没有全国统一的规划，而是像约瑟夫的彩衣一样，各家各户拼凑而成。每个城市的工程师都设计了自己的设备，并按需生产。此外，每家公司都依法被限制在六英里半径的范围内，因此荷兰遍布着一个个小巧的系统，没有两个是相同的。比利时自1893年以来就实行政府体制，因此具有统一性，但却缺乏企业精神。工厂陈旧且规模太小。西班牙拥有私营公司，为两万人口提供相当不错的服务。罗马尼亚的公司数量只有西班牙的一半。葡萄牙在里斯本和波尔图各有两家小型公司。希腊、塞尔维亚和保加利亚各有两千家公司。冰天雪地的冰岛的公司数量只有西班牙的四分之一；甚至在土耳其——这片在旧苏丹统治时期是禁地的地方——青年土耳其党人也开始进口电话机和铜线。

    The main peculiarity in Holland is that there is no national plan, but rather a patchwork, that resembles Joseph's coat of many colors. Each city engineer has designed his own type of apparatus and had it made to order. Also, each company is fenced in by law within a six-mile circle, so that Holland is dotted with thumb-nail systems, no two of which are alike. In Belgium there has been a government system since 1893, hence there is unity, but no enterprise. The plant is old-fashioned and too small. Spain has private companies, which give fairly good service to twenty thousand people. Roumania has half as many. Portugal has two small companies in Lisbon and Oporto. Greece, Servia, and Bulgaria have a scanty two thousand apiece. The frozen little isle of Iceland has one-quarter as many; and even into Turkey, which was a forbidden land under the regime of the old Sultan, the Young Turks are importing boxes of telephones and coils of copper wire.

    欧洲只有一个国家真正领略了电话的魅力——那就是瑞典。瑞典的电话发展可谓一帆风顺，邮政部门并未过多干预；更重要的是，瑞典拥有一位极具魄力和能力的商业领袖，他就是亨利·塞德格伦。如果让他成为欧洲的电话之王，历史将会截然不同。凭借他坚持不懈的努力，斯德哥尔摩成为了美国以外电话普及率最高的城市。在他的推动下，瑞典的电话普及率达到了16.5万部，位列欧洲第四。然而，自他去世后，美国政府却推出了一套与瑞典电话系统完全相同的方案，由此引发了一场愈演愈烈、愈发荒谬的战争。

    There is one European country, and only one, which has caught the telephone spirit--Sweden. Here telephony had a free swinging start. It was let alone by the Post Office; and better still, it had a Man, a business-builder of remarkable force and ability, named Henry Cedergren. Had this man been made the Telephone-Master of Europe, there would have been a different story to tell. By his insistent enterprise he made Stockholm the best telephoned city outside of the United States. He pushed his country forward until, having one hundred and sixty-five thousand telephones, it stood fourth among the European nations. Since his death the Government has entered the field with a duplicate system, and a war has been begun which grows yearly more costly and absurd.

    亚洲拥有八亿五千万人口，但电话数量却比费城还少，其中四分之三的电话都集中在日本这个小岛国。日本人从一开始就对电话充满热情。1883年，东京就有一个繁忙的电话交换局。如今，这个交换局的用户已达两万五千人，如果不是受到政府特殊政策的限制，用户数量还会更多。负责运营电话系统的公务员都是能干的人。他们收费合理，并为国家赚取百分之十的利润。但他们的电话服务却无法满足不断增长的需求。公共所有制最令人匪夷所思的现象之一，就是如今东京竟然有八千名市民在排队等候安装电话，他们愿意付费却无法安装。而且，当一位东京市民去世时，如果他生前拥有电话特许经营权，通常会被列入遗嘱，作为一项价值四百美元的财产。

    Asia, as yet, with her eight hundred and fifty million people, has fewer telephones than Philadelphia, and three-fourths of them are in the tiny island of Japan. The Japanese were enthusiastic telephonists from the first. They had a busy exchange in Tokio in 1883. This has now grown to have twenty-five thousand users, and might have more, if it had not been stunted by the peculiar policy of the Government. The public officials who operate the system are able men. They charge a fair price and make ten per cent profit for the State. But they do not keep pace with the demand. It is one of the oddest vagaries of public ownership that there is now in Tokio a WAITING LIST of eight thousand citizens, who are offering to pay for telephones and cannot get them. And when a Tokian dies, his franchise to a telephone, if he has one, is usually itemized in his will as a four-hundred- dollar property.

    在亚洲排名第二的印度，电话数量不超过九千部——平均每三万三千人才拥有一部！事实上，这还不如纽约五座摩天大楼里的电话数量多。荷属东印度群岛和中国各自只有七千部电话，但中国最近在电话普及方面取得了进展。政府将拨款两千万美元用于建设全国性的电话和电报系统。北京正满怀惊奇地指向一座崭新的交换局，它配备了两台拥有数万根线的交换机。广州、汉口和天津等地也在建设类似的交换局。最终，电话将在中国蓬勃发展，就像它在旧金山华人区一样。中国皇后在北京之围后下令在她的宫殿里安装一部电话，就在她坐龙宝座的触手可及之处；她对任何从事“闪电般快速通话”（中国人对电话的称呼）业务的代表都非常友好。

    India, which is second on the Asiatic list, has no more than nine thousand telephones--one to every thirty-three thousand of her population! Not quite so many, in fact, as there are in five of the skyscrapers of New York. The Dutch East Indies and China have only seven thousand apiece, but in China there has recently come a forward movement. A fund of twenty million dollars is to be spent in constructing a national system of telephone and telegraph. Peking is now pointing with wonder and delight to a new exchange, spick and span, with a couple of ten-thousand-wire switchboards. Others are being built in Canton, Hankow, and Tien-Tsin. Ultimately, the telephone will flourish in China, as it has done in the Chinese quarter in San Francisco. The Empress of China, after the siege of Peking, commanded that a telephone should be hung in her palace, within reach of her dragon throne; and she was very friendly with any representative of the "Speaking Lightning Sounds" business, as the Chinese term telephony.

    在波斯，电话的出现颇具滑稽剧色彩。一位新沙阿信心过头，在宫殿和德黑兰集市之间架设了一条电话线，并邀请民众随时与他沟通诉说不满。民众果然畅所欲言！他们说话如此自由，言辞如此粗俗，以至于沙阿下令军队攻击他们。他向新成立的议会开火，随即被愤怒的民众赶出了波斯。由此可见，电话在波斯应该很受欢迎，尽管目前波斯只有不到二十部电话在使用。

    In Persia the telephone made its entry recently in true comic-opera fashion. A new Shah, in an outburst of confidence, set up a wire between his palace and the market-place in Teheran, and invited his people to talk to him whenever they had grievances. And they talked! They talked so freely and used such language, that the Shah ordered out his soldiers and attacked them. He fired upon the new Parliament, and was at once chased out of Persia by the enraged people. From this it would appear that the telephone ought to be popular in Persia, although at present there are not more than twenty in use.

    除了布宜诺斯艾利斯以外，南美洲的电话很少，可能不超过三万部。巴西的佩德罗国王在百年庆典上与贝尔结为好友，并于1881年将电话引入巴西；但三十年来，巴西的电话用户数量始终不足一万。加拿大和瑞典的电话用户数量相同，均为十六万五千部。墨西哥可能有一万部电话；新西兰两万六千部；澳大利亚五万五千部。

    South America, outside of Buenos Ayres, has few telephones, probably not more than thirty thousand. Dom Pedro of Brazil, who befriended Bell at the Centennial, introduced telephony into his country in 1881; but it has not in thirty years been able to obtain ten thousand users. Canada has exactly the same number as Sweden--one hundred and sixty-five thousand. Mexico has perhaps ten thousand; New Zealand twenty-six thousand; and Australia fifty- five thousand.

    在各大洲的排名中，非洲显得格外靠后。北部的埃及和阿尔及利亚拥有12000个城镇；南部的英属南非也拥有同样多的城镇；而在两者之间广袤的地带，城镇数量也仅有寥寥几千个。任何深入中非的人，至今仍能听到木鼓的敲击声，那是当地土著居民用手语交流的方式。在刚果地区，有一根铜线，是已故比利时国王下令架设的。架设这根铜线或许是电话线工人历史上最冒险的壮举。这条线路长达750英里，穿过中部丛林。白蚁啃食着木杆，野象拔起铁杆。猴子在电线上嬉戏，野蛮人偷走电线做箭头。但这条线路最终还是架设完毕，如今，人们仍然在谈论橡胶和象牙。

    Far down in the list of continents stands Africa. Egypt and Algeria have twelve thousand at the north; British South Africa has as many at the south; and in the vast stretches between there are barely a thousand more. Whoever pushes into Central Africa will still hear the beat of the wooden drum, which is the clattering sign-language of the natives. One strand of copper wire there is, through the Congo region, placed there by order of the late King of Belgium. To string it was probably the most adventurous piece of work in the history of telephone linemen. There was one seven hundred and fifty mile stretch of the central jungle. There were white ants that ate the wooden poles, and wild elephants that pulled up the iron poles. There were monkeys that played tag on the lines, and savages that stole the wire for arrow- heads. But the line was carried through, and to-day is alive with conversations concerning rubber and ivory.

    所以，我们几乎可以说，电话“无所不在，无所不包”。在阿比西尼亚，电话线长达一千英里；在斐济群岛，也有一百五十英里。粗略估计，如今全球共有一千万部电话，雇佣了二十五万人，需要两千一百万英里的电话线，总成本高达一千五亿美元，每年承载着一千四十亿次通话。所有这一切，而当年听到电话最初微弱声音的人们，如今依然健在，而且年纪也不小了。

    So, we may almost say of the telephone that "there is no speech nor language where its voice is not heard." There are even a thousand miles of its wire in Abyssinia and one hundred and fifty miles in the Fiji Islands. Roughly speaking, there are now ten million telephones in all countries, employing two hundred and fifty thousand people, requiring twenty-one million miles of wire, representing a cost of fifteen hundred million dollars, and carrying fourteen thousand million conversations a year. All this, and yet the men who heard the first feeble cry of the in- fant telephone are still alive, and not by any means old.

    没有哪个国家的电话普及率能达到美国的水平。美国每百人拥有八部电话，而其他任何国家都达不到美国的一半。加拿大位居第二，每百人拥有近四部电话；瑞典排名第三。德国的电话数量与纽约州相当；英国的电话数量与俄亥俄州相当。芝加哥的电话数量超过伦敦；波士顿的电话数量是巴黎的两倍。整个欧洲，包括其二十个国家，电话数量仅为美国的三分之一。按人口比例计算，欧洲的电话数量仅为美国的十三分之一。

    No foreign country has reached the high American level of telephony. The United States has eight telephones per hundred of population, while no other country has one-half as many. Canada stands second, with almost four per hundred; and Sweden is third. Germany has as many telephones as the State of New York; and Great Britain as many as Ohio. Chicago has more than London; and Boston twice as many as Paris. In the whole of Europe, with her twenty nations, there are one- third as many telephones as in the United States. In proportion to her population, Europe has only one-thirteenth as many.

    美国写信的数量只有欧洲的一半，电报发送量只有欧洲的三分之一，但打电话的频率却是欧洲的两倍。欧洲家庭平均每年发送三封电报，每周发送三封信和一条电话留言；而美国家庭平均每年发送五封电报，每周发送七封信和十一条电话留言。这个国家仅占地球面积的6%，人口占世界总人口的5%，却拥有全球70%的电话。而全球一半的电话业务，也就是一半，都由美国的贝尔系统掌控。

    The United States writes half as many letters as Europe, sends one-third as many telegrams, and talks twice as much at the telephone. The average European family sends three telegrams a year, and three letters and one telephone message a week; while the average American family sends five telegrams a year, and seven letters and eleven telephone messages a week. This one na- tion, which owns six per cent of the earth and is five per cent of the human race, has SEVENTY per cent of the telephones. And fifty per cent, or one-half, of the telephony of the world, is now comprised in the Bell System of this country.

    欧洲只有六个国家电话普及率较高——德国、英国、瑞典、丹麦、挪威和瑞士。其他国家每百人拥有的电话不足一部。小小的丹麦比奥地利还多。小小的芬兰的服务比法国好。比利时的电话最贵，每部273美元；芬兰的电话最便宜，每部81美元。但比利时的一部电话的收入是挪威的三倍。总的来说，欧洲的经验表明，电话的普及程度取决于一个国家如何看待它。它的实用性取决于人们如何明智地使用它，以及他们如何积极主动地使用它。它可以成为一项宝贵的资产，也可以成为一种负担。

    There are only six nations in Europe that make a fair showing--the Germans, British, Swedish, Danes, Norwegians, and Swiss. The others have less than one telephone per hundred. Little Denmark has more than Austria. Little Finland has better service than France. The Belgian telephones have cost the most--two hundred and seventy-three dollars apiece; and the Finnish telephones the least--eighty-one dollars. But a telephone in Belgium earns three times as much as one in Norway. In general, the lesson in Europe is this, that the telephone is what a nation makes it. Its usefulness depends upon the sense and enterprise with which it is handled. It may be either an invaluable asset or a nuisance.

    政府权力过大！这正是大多数国家失败的根本原因。在电话发明之前，电报是国家垄断的；而电话也被视为电报的一种形式。政府官员们没有意识到，电话系统是一个高度复杂的技术问题，更像是钢琴厂或钢铁厂。因此，每当有民众建立起电话服务时，政府官员都会虎视眈眈，通常会将其夺走。于是，电话就成了电报的一部分，电报又是邮局的一部分，邮局又是政府的一部分。它只是官僚机构中微不足道的一小部分——一个微不足道的枝桠。在这样的环境下，电话不可能发展壮大。它能存活下来，本身就是一个奇迹。

    Too much government! That has been the basic reason for failure in most countries. Before the telephone was invented, the telegraph had been made a State monopoly; and the tele- phone was regarded as a species of telegraph. The public officials did not see that a telephone system is a highly complex and technical problem, much more like a piano factory or a steel- mill. And so, wherever a group of citizens established a telephone service, the government officials looked upon it with jealous eyes, and usually snatched it away. The telephone thus became a part of the telegraph, which is a part of the post office, which is a part of the government. It is a fraction of a fraction of a fraction --a mere twig of bureaucracy. Under such conditions the telephone could not prosper. The wonder is that it survived.

    如果按照美国模式来发展，国外的电话水平可以提升到美国的水平。失败并非出于种族原因。服务缓慢和操作失误，是把电话当作道路或消防部门来对待的必然结果；任何一个国家，只要对电话有正确的认识，敢于将其交给称职的人员，并投入足够的资金，就能获得人们梦寐以求的快捷高效的服务。有些国家已经开始行动了。中国、日本和法国都曾派遣代表团前往纽约——“电话之都”，学习最先进的电话技术。甚至连俄罗斯也已经从官僚手中解放了电话，现在正免费向有进取心的人提供这项服务。

    Handled on the American plan, the telephone abroad may be raised to American levels. There is no racial reason for failure. The slow service and the bungling are the natural results of treating the telephone as though it were a road or a fire department; and any nation that rises to a proper conception of the telephone, that dares to put it into competent hands and to strengthen it with enough capital, can secure as alert and brisk a service as heart can wish. Some nations are already on the way. China, Japan, and France have sent delegations to New York City --"the Mecca of telephone men," to learn the art of telephony in its highest development. Even Russia has rescued the telephone from her bureaucrats and is now offering it freely to men of enterprise.

    在大多数国家，电话服务正稳步提升速度。“廉价劣质”电话的风潮正在消退；而电话首先是一种速度工具的理念正逐渐被人们接受。速度更快、收费翻倍的长途电话服务广受欢迎。发展缓慢的国家正在逐渐认识到时间的价值，而这正是电话服务带来的第一课。我们的收割机和割草机如今已销往75个国家。我们的有轨电车已遍布各大城市。摩洛哥正在进口我们价值1美元的手表；韩国正在体会到九个人共用一把铲子会造成资源浪费。而这一切都离不开电话。

    In most foreign countries telephone service is being steadily geared up to a faster pace. The craze for "cheap and nasty" telephony is passing; and the idea that the telephone is above all else a SPEED instrument, is gaining ground. A faster long-distance service, at double rates, is being well patronized. Slow-moving races are learning the value of time, which is the first lesson in telephony. Our reapers and mowers now go to seventy-five nations. Our street cars run in all great cities. Morocco is importing our dollar watches; Korea is learning the waste of allowing nine men to dig with one spade. And all this means telephones.

    三十年来，西电公司已向海外销售了价值六千七百万美元的电话设备。但这仅仅是个开始。要在中国实现每百人一部电话，就需要三亿美元的投入。要让欧洲拥有与美国目前一样完善的设备，则需要三千万部电话，以及与之配套的线路和交换机。虽然在许多国家，普及电话尚未成为现实，但在文明的不断推进下，这一天迟早会到来。

    In thirty years, the Western Electric has sold sixty-seven million dollars' worth of telephonic apparatus to foreign countries. But this is no more than a fair beginning. To put one telephone in China to every hundred people will mean an outlay of three hundred million dollars. To give Europe as fit an equipment as the United States now has, will mean thirty million telephones, with proper wire and switchboards to match. And while telephony for the masses is not yet a live question in many countries, sooner or later, in the relentless push of civilization, it must come.

    或许，在遥远的未来，各国和平友好，各国各尽其所能地为其他国家服务时，美国将被公认为电话领域的技术和权威之源。届时，美国或许会像如今供应石油、钢铁、铁轨和农用机械一样，受邀重建或运营其他国家的电话系统。正如今日精明的买家会向法国采购香槟，向德国采购玩具，向英国采购棉布，向东方采购地毯一样，他们终将把美国视为电话的天然家园和总部。

    Possibly, in that far future of peace and goodwill among nations, when each country does for all the others what it can do best, the United States may be generally recognized as the source of skill and authority on telephony. It may be called in to rebuild or operate the telephone systems of other countries, in the same way that it is now supplying oil and steel rails and farm machinery. Just as the wise buyer of to-day asks France for champagne, Germany for toys, England for cottons, and the Orient for rugs, so he will learn to look upon the United States as the natural home and headquarters of the telephone.

    第九章 电话的未来

    CHAPTER IX. THE FUTURE OF THE TELEPHONE

    1907年春天，西奥多·N·韦尔，一位身材魁梧、面色红润、头发花白的男子，正在佛蒙特州北部监督一座大型谷仓的建造。他的房子就在附近，坐落在起伏的山坡上，俯瞰着林登镇，远眺常绿森林之外的伯克山巍峨耸立。他的农场面积近十平方英里，位于房子后方，是一片椭圆形的田野和林地，空地上散落着几十间小屋。他的威尔士矮种马和瑞士牛正在五月的青草上悠闲地吃草，工人们则忙着耕犁、耙地和播种。距离他上次受邀创建电话行业的商业架构并制定其总体发展规划，已经过去了近三十年。此后，他还从事过许多其他工作。布宜诺斯艾利斯市仅仅因为他为该市提供了有轨电车和电灯系统，就付给他的报酬比美国因他将电话商业化而付给他的报酬还要多。如今他已功成名就，退休了，可以自由自在地享受农场的乐趣，忘却城市和电话带来的种种烦恼。

    In the Spring of 1907 Theodore N. Vail, a rugged, ruddy, white-haired man, was superintending the building of a big barn in northern Vermont. His house stood near-by, on a balcony of rolling land that overlooked the town of Lyndon and far beyond, across evergreen forests to the massive bulk of Burke Mountain. His farm, very nearly ten square miles in area, lay back of the house in a great oval of field and woodland, with several dozen cottages in the clearings. His Welsh ponies and Swiss cattle were grazing on the May grass, and the men were busy with the ploughs and harrows and seeders. It was almost thirty years since he had been called in to create the business structure of telephony, and to shape the general plan of its development. Since then he had done many other things. The one city of Buenos Ayres had paid him more, merely for giving it a system of trolleys and electric lights, than the United States had paid him for putting the telephone on a business basis. He was now rich and retired, free to enjoy his play-work of the farm and to forget the troubles of the city and the telephone

    但就在他站在谷仓建造工人们中间时，一群来自波士顿和纽约的电话公司董事代表团来了。他们大多是电话行业的“老派人物”。在电话行业的开拓时期，他们曾与韦尔并肩作战；如今，他们前来邀请他重返电话行业，结束他二十年的沉寂。韦尔对这个提议嗤之以鼻。

    But, as he stood among his barn-builders, there arrived from Boston and New York a delegation of telephone directors. Most of them belonged to the "Old Guard" of telephony. They had fought under Vail in the pioneer days; and now they had come to ask him to return to the telephone business, after twenty years of absence. Vail laughed at the suggestion.

    “胡说，”他说，“我太老了，我都六十二岁了。”董事们坚持不懈。他们谈到恐慌的阴云即将笼罩，需要另一位强有力的领导人来掌舵，直到危机过去，但韦尔仍然拒绝。他们谈起往事和回忆，但他摇了摇头。“我这辈子，”他说，“都想当个农民。”

    "Nonsense," he said, "I'm too old. I'm sixty- two years of age." The directors persisted. They spoke of the approaching storm-cloud of panic and the need of another strong hand at the wheel until the crisis was over, but Vail still refused. They spoke of old times and old memories, but he shook his head. "All my life," he said, "I have wanted to be a farmer."

    然后，他们向他展示了当时的电话现状。他们告诉他，他规划的“宏伟电话系统”尚未完成。他是这个系统的设计者，而它却功亏一篑。电话行业当时蓬勃发展，欣欣向荣。在弗雷德里克·P·菲什的卓越领导下，电话行业飞速发展。但这距离韦尔年轻时梦想的那个系统还相差甚远；因此，当董事们把那份未完成的计划摆在他面前时，他选择了妥协。他天性追求完美，这种本能驱使他同意了。这就是电话的召唤。

    Then they drew a picture of the telephone situation. They showed him that the "grand telephonic system" which he had planned was unfinished. He was its architect, and it was undone. The telephone business was energetic and prosperous. Under the brilliant leadership of Frederick P. Fish, it had grown by leaps and bounds. But it was still far from being the SYSTEM that Vail had dreamed of in his younger days; and so, when the directors put before him his unfinished plan, he surrendered. The instinct for completeness, which is one of the dominating characteristics of his mind, compelled him to consent. It was the call of the telephone.

    自1907年5月的那个早晨以来，电话和电报界的先驱们取得了巨大的成就。贝尔系统毫发无损地度过了恐慌时期。在疑虑和混乱最为严重的时候，韦尔以他务实而朴实的农夫风格，给股东们写了一封公开信。他在信中写道：

    Since that May morning, 1907, great things have been done by the men of the telephone and telegraph world. The Bell System was brought through the panic without a scratch. When the doubt and confusion were at their worst, Vail wrote an open letter to his stock-holders, in his practical, farmer-like way. He said:

    “过去十个月，我们的净收入为1371.5万美元，而1906年同期为1157.9万美元。我们目前在银行有超过1800万美元的存款；而且我们两年内不需要借任何钱。”

    "Our net earnings for the last ten months were $13,715,000, as against $11,579,000 for the same period in 1906. We have now in the banks over $18,000,000; and we will not need to borrow any money for two years."

    不久之后，整合工作便开始了。业务重叠的公司被合并。数千个小型地方线路集群被接入全国线路。公开透明的政策取代了专利诉讼时期自然而然养成的保密习惯。访客和记者可以自由出入。教育广告刊登在最受欢迎的杂志上。发明家们被激励着去攻克长途传输难题。作为交换，一家历史悠久的西部联合公司的控制权从杰伊·古尔德的子女手中转移到了美国电话电报公司的三万名股东手中，而这笔交易的金额高达三千万美元。

    Soon afterwards, the work of consolidation began. Companies that overlapped were united. Small local wire-clusters, several thousands of them, were linked to the national lines. A policy of publicity superseded the secrecy which had naturally grown to be a habit in the days of patent litigation. Visitors and reporters found an open door. Educational advertisements were published in the most popular magazines. The corps of inventors was spurred up to conquer the long-distance problems. And in return for a thirty million check, the control of the historic Western Union was transferred from the children of Jay Gould to the thirty thousand stock-holders of the American Telephone and Telegraph Company.

    因此，根据已完成的工作，我们可以对电话的未来做出一些推测。三十年前，除了韦尔的想象之外，这个“宏伟的电话系统”还不存在，如今似乎即将成为现实。就连街头的报童都在为此奔走呼号。当然，目前还没有一个完美的电话系统蓝图，但我们现在已经能够大致了解韦尔计划的轮廓。

    From what has been done, therefore, we may venture a guess as to the future of the telephone. This "grand telephonic system" which had no existence thirty years ago, except in the imagination of Vail, seems to be at hand. The very newsboys in the streets are crying it. And while there is, of course, no exact blueprint of a best possible telephone system, we can now see the general outlines of Vail's plan.

    这个计划既不神秘也不可怕，与华尔街的阴谋诡计毫无关系。除了那些纸面公司的发起人之外，没有人会被挤出局。事实很简单，韦尔之所以要建立一个完整的贝尔系统，原因和他为他的瑞士牛和威尔士小马建造一个宽敞舒适的谷仓，而不是六个狭小简陋的棚子一样。他从来都不是那种靠别人的损失来牟利的“金融大亨”。他只是把农民经营农场时所秉持的务实精神运用到了电话业务中。他正在为电话和电报建造一个象征性的“大谷仓”。

    There is nothing mysterious or ominous in this plan. It has nothing to do with the pools and conspiracies of Wall Street. No one will be squeezed out except the promoters of paper companies. The simple fact is that Vail is organizing a complete Bell System for the same reason that he built one big comfortable barn for his Swiss cattle and his Welsh ponies, instead of half a dozen small uncomfortable sheds. He has never been a "high financier" to juggle profits out of other men's losses. He is merely applying to the telephone business the same hard sense that any farmer uses in the management of his farm. He is building a Big Barn, metaphorically, for the telephone and telegraph.

    显然，未来的电话系统将是全国性的，这样同一国家内的任何两个人都能互相通话。它不会是竞争性的，因为没有哪个农民会想到以竞争的方式经营自己的农场。它将采用类似军事术语的“人员和线路”组织结构。每个地方公司将继续处理本地事务，并充分发挥自助互助的基本美德。但同时也会像现在一样，设立一个中央专家机构来处理所有公司共同面临的重大事务。一方面不搞分裂或脱离，另一方面也不搞官僚主义——这正是理想电话系统所秉持的典型美国理念。

    Plainly, the telephone system of the future will be national, so that any two people in the same country will be able to talk to one another. It will not be competitive, for the reason that no farmer would think for a moment of running his farm on competitive lines. It will have a staff- and-line organization, to use a military phrase. Each local company will continue to handle its own local affairs, and exercise to the full the basic virtue of self-help. But there will also be, as now, a central body of experts to handle the larger affairs that are common to all companies. No separateness or secession on the one side, nor bureaucracy on the other--that is the typically American idea that underlies the ideal telephone system.

    在这种体系下，权力层级将从地方经理开始，向上依次是州属公司的董事；再向上是国家公司的董事；最终，凌驾于所有公司领导人之上，直至联邦政府本身。许多外国政府所有制电话的失败并不意味着私营公司将拥有绝对权力。恰恰相反。三十年的经验表明，私营电话公司往往比政府部门更能服从民意。但民主的一条基本原则是，任何公司，无论经营多么良好，都不能在不对其自身行为承担严格责任的情况下控制公共设施。随着政治从一场游戏转变为一项责任，未来的电话无疑将由某种公共委员会监督，该委员会将有权处理投诉，并防止重复收费和虚假宣传等扰民行为。

    The line of authority, in such a system, will begin with the local manager. From him it will rise to the directors of the State company; then higher still to the directors of the national company; and finally, above all corporate leaders to the Federal Government itself. The failure of government ownership of the telephone in so many foreign countries does not mean that the private companies will have absolute power. Quite the reverse. The lesson of thirty years' experience shows that a private telephone company is apt to be much more obedient to the will of the people than if it were a Government de- partment. But it is an axiom of democracy that no company, however well conducted, will be permitted to control a public convenience without being held strictly responsible for its own acts. As politics becomes less of a game and more of a responsibility, the telephone of the future will doubtless be supervised by some sort of public committee, which will have power to pass upon complaints, and to prevent the nuisance of duplication and the swindle of watering stock.

    随着联邦监管日益高效，人们对垄断的担忧将会减少，就像铁路行业的情况一样。事实上，尽管现在人们大多已经忘记，但美国最初的铁路在长达十年或更长时间的时间里都是按照反垄断政策运营的。铁轨对所有人免费开放。任何拥有带轮缘车轮的马车的人都可以驾驶它在铁轨上行驶，与火车竞争。当时火车和货车混杂在一起，热闹非凡，速度最慢的车辆总是拖慢速度；这种情况在一些铁路上一直持续到1857年。到那时，人们意识到在铁路上进行竞争是荒谬的。他们允许每条线路由一家公司垄断，铁路扩张的时代由此开始。

    As this Federal supervision becomes more and more efficient, the present fear of monopoly will decrease, just as it did in the case of the railways. It is a fact, although now generally forgotten, that the first railways of the United States were run for ten years or more on an anti-monopoly plan. The tracks were free to all. Any one who owned a cart with flanged wheels could drive it on the rails and compete with the locomotives. There was a happy-go-lucky jumble of trains and wagons, all held back by the slowest team; and this continued on some railways until as late as 1857. By that time the people saw that com- petition on a railway track was absurd. They allowed each track to be monopolized by one company, and the era of expansion began.

    当然，现在没有人会为独立货车司机的消亡感到惋惜。他比任何铁路公司都更加专断，收费也更高；随着国家的发展，他变得越来越难以为继。他并非最适合生存的群体。为了公共利益，人们限制他与铁路竞争，并教他与铁路合作，负责往返车站的货物运输。令他惊讶的是，他发现这种合作方式更加有利可图，也更加愉快。他被挤出了一个糟糕的工作岗位，进入了一个好岗位。通过类似的演变过程，美国正在迅速超越小型独立电话公司。这些电话公司最终也会像货车司机一样，通过与主流电话系统连接，逐步提升自身的社会价值。

    No one, certainly, at the present time, regrets the passing of the independent teamster. He was much more arbitrary and expensive than any railroad has ever dared to be; and as the country grew, he became impossible. He was not the fittest to survive. For the general good, he was held back from competing with the railroad, and taught to cooperate with it by hauling freight to and from the depots. This, to his surprise, he found much more profitable and pleasant. He had been squeezed out of a bad job into a good one. And by a similar process of evolution, the United States is rapidly outgrowing the small independent telephone companies. These will eventually, one by one, rise as the teamster did to a higher social value, by clasping wires with the main system of telephony.

    直到1881年，贝尔系统一直由一个家族集团掌控，是一家纯粹的私人企业。公司成立之初曾邀请公众参与，但遭到拒绝。1881年后，贝尔系统转由小股东控制，并一直延续至今。如今，它已成为我们最民主化的企业之一，向超过十万个家庭发放工资或股息。它有时或许带有排他性，但从未低俗不堪。它从未盲目追求金钱，也从未被股票投机的狂热所裹挟。它始终保持着一种人性化的情怀。即使在今天，美国电话电报公司的每一张支票上仍然印着一位俊俏的丘比特，他坐在椅子上，椅子上放着一本厚厚的书，正兴高采烈地对着电话喋喋不休。

    Until 1881 the Bell System was in the hands of a family group. It was a strictly private enterprise. The public had been asked to help in its launching, and had refused. But after 1881 it passed into the control of the small stock-holders, and has remained there without a break. It is now one of our most democratized businesses, scattering either wages or dividends into more than a hundred thousand homes. It has at times been exclusive, but never sordid. It has never been dollar-mad, nor frenzied by the virus of stock-gambling. There has always been a vein of sentiment in it that kept it in touch with human nature. Even at the present time, each check of the American Telephone and Telegraph Company carries on it a picture of a pretty Cupid, sitting on a chair upon which he has placed a thick book, and gayly prattling into a telephone.

    随着贝尔系统和西联公司携手合作，预计在不久的将来将出现几项意义深远的变革。仅凭一项协议，就有五百万电话用户被纳入西联公司的信用账户；贝尔公司的每个电话局现在都兼作电报局。三条电话留言和八份电报可以通过两对电线同时发送：这是近期科学的一项奇迹，现在正进行大规模的测试。大部分长途电话线，总长达两百万英里，都可以用于电报传输；而西联公司三分之一的电线，长五十万英里，稍加改造即可用于通话。

    Several sweeping changes may be expected in the near future, now that there is team-play between the Bell System and the Western Union. Already, by a stroke of the pen, five million users of telephones have been put on the credit books of the Western Union; and every Bell telephone office is now a telegraph office. Three telephone messages and eight telegrams may be sent AT THE SAME TIME over two pairs of wires: that is one of the recent miracles of science, and is now to be tried out upon a gigantic scale. Most of the long-distance telephone wires, fully two million miles, can be used for telegraphic purposes; and a third of the Western Union wires, five hundred thousand miles, may with a few changes be used for talking.

    西联公司租用了22500个办公地点，所有这些开支都使得电报成为少数人的奢侈品。它雇佣的信使人数与当年随谢尔曼将军从亚特兰大一路征战到海边的军队人数相当。如果贝尔电报线和莫尔斯电报线能够连接到同一个终端，并且可以通过电话收发电报，那么这两项开支都将大幅减少。此外，或许最大的好处是，可以将那些在街头奔波的信使从街头带走，送他们去上学或学习一门有用的技能。

    The Western Union is paying rent for twenty- two thousand, five hundred offices, all of which helps to make telegraphy a luxury of the few. It is employing as large a force of messenger- boys as the army that marched with General Sherman from Atlanta to the sea. Both of these items of expense will dwindle when a Bell wire and a Morse wire can be brought to a common terminal; and when a telegram can be received or delivered by telephone. There will also be a gain, perhaps the largest of all, in removing the trudging little messenger-boy from the streets and sending him either to school or to learn some useful trade.

    事实上，美国是第一个成功地将电话和电报发展到合理水平的国家。

    The fact is that the United States is the first country that has succeeded in putting both telephone and telegraph upon the proper basis.

    在其他地方，要么两者相去甚远，要么电话仅仅是电报部门的附属工具。根据美国的新理念，两者并非竞争关系，而是互补关系。邮局寄送包裹；电报发送包裹的内容；而电话本身并不发送任何东西。它是一种使分隔两地的人能够进行对话的设备。这三者各自拥有独特的领域，因此它们之间从未产生过任何嫉妒或敌对关系。

    Elsewhere either the two are widely apart, or the telephone is a mere adjunct of a telegraphic department. According to the new American plan, the two are not competitive, but complementary. The one is a supplement to the other. The post office sends a package; the telegraph sends the contents of the package; but the telephone sends nothing. It is an apparatus that makes conversation possible between two separated people. Each of the three has a distinct field of its own, so that there has never been any cause for jealousy among them.

    将电话视为邮局或电报的附属机构已是荒谬之举。如今，全世界通过电话发送的信息量几乎与通过信件发送的信息量相当；而电话通话量更是电报的32倍。在美国，电话已发展成为电报的“老大哥”。它的净收入是电报的六倍，线路长度是电报的八倍。而且，它传输的信息量与电报、信件和铁路客运量的总和相当。

    To make the telephone an annex of the post office or the telegraph has become absurd. There are now in the whole world very nearly as many messages sent by telephone as by letter; and there are THIRT-TWO TIMES as many telephone calls as telegrams. In the United States, the telephone has grown to be the big brother of the telegraph. It has six times the net earnings and eight times the wire. And it transmits as many messages as the combined total of telegrams, letters, and railroad passengers.

    这种普遍存在的整合趋势带来了一系列问题，这些问题将在未来许多年里吸引电话行业最杰出的人才去思考。如何在不承受组织弊端的情况下获得组织的优势，如何在保持敏捷性的同时增强实力，如何在保持系统性的同时又不失昔日的魄力和勇气，如何在不失去对整体形势的全局把握的情况下将员工队伍培养成一支高效率的专业队伍——这些都是新一代电话从业者必须找到答案的难题。它们也展现了电话行业能够为当今雄心勃勃、才华横溢的年轻人提供的艰巨任务。

    This universal trend toward consolidation has introduced a variety of problems that will engage the ablest brains in the telephone world for many years to come. How to get the benefits of organization without its losses, to become strong without losing quickness, to become systematic without losing the dash and dare of earlier days, to develop the working force into an army of high-speed specialists without losing the bird's- eye view of the whole situation,--these are the riddles of the new type, for which the telephonists of the next generation must find the answers. They illustrate the nature of the big jobs that the telephone has to offer to an ambitious and gifted young man of to-day.

    “问题从来没有像现在这样庞大和复杂，”电话工程师主管JJ Carty说道。宏大构想与微小构想之间的永恒斗争依然存在——那些着眼于未来愿景的人与那些只关注现状的人之间的斗争仍在继续。打破纪录的竞赛仍在进行。如今，接线员只需30秒就能找到要找的人。这比早期中央电话公司耗时缩短了十分之一；但这仍然太长了。这相当于宝贵的半分钟。必须将其缩短到25秒，或者20秒，甚至15秒。

    "The problems never were as large or as complex as they are right now," says J. J. Carty, the chief of the telephone engineers. The eternal struggle remains between the large and little ideas--between the men who see what might be and the men who only see what IS. There is still the race to break records. Already the girl at the switchboard can find the person wanted in thirty seconds. This is one-tenth of the time that was taken in the early centrals; but it is still too long. It is one-half of a valuable minute. It must be cut to twenty-five seconds, or twenty or fifteen.

    发明家们仍在为突破距离的极限而努力。通话距离已从20英里增加到2500英里，但这还远远不够。有些文明人相隔万里，却有着共同的利益。例如，在中国义和团运动期间，一些身在北京的美国人甚至愿意倾尽所有，只为能用上一两根电线与纽约通话。

    There is still the inventors' battle to gain miles. The distance over which conversations can be held has been increased from twenty miles to twenty-five hundred. But this is not far enough. There are some civilized human beings who are twelve thousand miles apart, and who have interests in common. During the Boxer Rebellion in China, for instance, there were Americans in Peking who would gladly have given half of their fortune for the use of a pair of wires to New York.

    在电话发明之初，贝尔就喜欢预言“终有一天，我们将跨越大西洋通话”；但这在当时被视为一种诗意的幻想，直到普平发明了自动推进电流的方法。自此以后，即使是最保守的工程师也会讨论跨大西洋电话传输的问题。至于诗人，他们如今梦想着有一天，人们可以开口说话，并听到自己的声音传到世​​界各地。

    In the earliest days of the telephone, Bell was fond of prophesying that "the time will come when we will talk across the Atlantic Ocean"; but this was regarded as a poetical fancy until Pupin invented his method of automatically propelling the electric current. Since then the most conservative engineer will discuss the problem of transatlantic telephony. And as for the poets, they are now dreaming of the time when a man may speak and hear his own voice come back to him around the world.

    眼下最紧迫的长途难题当然是如何从纽约向太平洋彼岸通话。如今，两大洋之间铁路运输只需三天半即可到达。西雅图正迫切希望架设一条通往东部的电报线路。圣地亚哥也希望在1915年巴拿马运河博览会之前就能用上。通往旧金山的电报线路已经铺设完毕，但以目前的技术水平还无法使用。而韦尔的团队正以惊人的速度赶工，力求为他送上一份生日礼物——让他从佛蒙特州的农场与整个大陆进行一次远程通话。

    The immediate long-distance problem is, of course, to talk from New York to the Pacific. The two oceans are now only three and a half days apart by rail. Seattle is clamoring for a wire to the East. San Diego wants one in time for her Panama Canal Exposition in 1915. The wires are already strung to San Francisco, but cannot be used in the present stage of the art. And Vail's captains are working now with almost breathless haste to give him a birthday present of a talk across the continent from his farm in Vermont.

    “我预见到美国在不久的将来会拥有一个通用的电话系统，”卡蒂说道。“西雅图的一条街道上矗立着西沃德的雕像，上面刻着‘致一个统一的国家’。但当一个东部人站在那里时，他会感受到这个遥远西部州的孤立感，这种感觉会一直伴随着他，直到他能够跨越美国的两端进行通话。至于我，”卡蒂继续说道，“我相信我们将能够跨越大陆和海洋进行通话。为什么不呢？一个人体内的细胞数量难道不比地球上的人口数量还要多吗？”

    "I can see a universal system of telephony for the United States in the very near future," says Carty. "There is a statue of Seward standing in one of the streets of Seattle. The inscription upon it is, `To a United Country.' But as an Easterner stands there, he feels the isolation of that Far Western State, and he will always feel it, until he can talk from one side of the United States to the other. For my part," con- tinues Carty, "I believe we will talk across continents and across oceans. Why not? Are there not more cells in one human body than there are people in the whole earth?"

    未来的卡蒂或许能解决单线传输的难题，通过恢复接地电路，将铜价削减一半。他或许能传输图像和语音。他或许能完善用于行驶列车的第三轨供电系统。他或许能构想出一种理想的绝缘材料，取代玻璃、云母、纸张和搪瓷。他或许能建立一套通用代码，使美国所有重要人物都拥有专属的索书号，以便像图书馆里的书籍一样，能够被迅速找到。

    Some future Carty may solve the abandoned problem of the single wire, and cut the copper bill in two by restoring the grounded circuit. He may transmit vision as well as speech. He may perfect a third-rail system for use on moving trains. He may conceive of an ideal insulating material to supersede glass, mica, paper, and enamel. He may establish a universal code, so that all persons of importance in the United States shall have call-numbers by which they may instantly be located, as books are in a library.

    或许会有其他年轻人创建业务范围广泛的商业部门，这项工作目前电话员的专业性还不足以胜任。无论谁来做这件事，都将是一位思维缜密、博学多才的人。他不仅精通电话技术，更能了解普通民众的生活。他会洞悉街头巷尾的闲言碎语、工会的诉求以及州长和总统的政策。他会关注西部农民的心理、日报的基调以及百货公司的经营之道。他的目标是洞悉公众舆论的微妙之处，并使电话服务适应时代变迁和需求的变化。他将使电话服务如同为人们量身定制的衣裳，完美契合人们的生活习惯。

    Some other young man may create a commercial department on wide lines, a work which telephone men have as yet been too specialized to do. Whoever does this will be a man of comprehensive brain. He will be as closely in touch with the average man as with the art of telephony. He will know the gossip of the street, the demands of the labor unions, and the policies of governors and presidents. The psy- chology of the Western farmer will concern him, and the tone of the daily press, and the methods of department stores. It will be his aim to know the subtle chemistry of public opinion, and to adapt the telephone service to the shifting moods and necessities of the times. HE WILL FIT TELEPHONY LIKE A GARMENT AROUND THE HABITS OF THE PEOPLE.

    此外，如今电话业务已发展壮大，其下一个重点必须是发挥优势而非弥补劣势。其座右铭必须是“Ich dien”（我服务）；未来电话行业的领军人物将致力于以各种实际方式诠释这一座右铭。他们将提供周到细致的服务，并不断解释说明。他们将持续开展教育，直至培养出一批精通电话技术的公众。他们将通过图片、讲座和展览进行教学。他们将在电话亭内悬挂图表，以便等待来电的人能够学习一些知识，并更愉快地度过时间。总之，他们将关注那些构成完美公共服务的无数细节。

    Also, now that the telephone business has become strong, its next anxiety must be to develop the virtues, and not the defects, of strength. Its motto must be "Ich dien"--I serve; and it will be the work of the future statesmen of the telephone to illustrate this motto in all its practical variations. They will cater and explain, and explain and cater. They will educate and educate, until they have created an expert public. They will teach by pictures and lectures and exhibitions. They will have charts and diagrams hung in the telephone booths, so that the person who is waiting for a call may learn a little and pass the time more pleasantly. They will, in a word, attend to those innumerable trifles that make the perfection of public service.

    贝尔系统在这方面已经走得很远了，他们建立了一个可以称之为“远见部门”的机构。这里聚集了业内的“预言家”。每当需要建设新的线路或交换机时，这些人都会着眼未来，研究当前形势。他们会制定一份“基本规划”，概述未来十五到二十年内可能发生的情况。他们无一例外都是乐观主义者。他们会为增长预留资金，但完全不考虑萎缩。在他们的建议下，贝尔公司各部门目前都储备了价值两千五百万美元的设备，等待着国家发展到需要这些设备的时候。即使在纽约市，也有一半的电缆管道是空的，这是为了迎接预计在1928年建成的拥有八百万人口的大纽约市。没有什么比一座新建的电话交换机更能体现务实的乐观和自信了，这座交换机三分之二的线路都已准备就绪，只待未来业务的开展。

    Already the Bell System has gone far in this direction by organizing what might fairly be called a foresight department. Here is where the fortune-tellers of the business sit. When new lines or exchanges are to be built, these men study the situation with an eye to the future. They prepare a "fundamental plan," outlining what may reasonably be expected to happen in fifteen or twenty years. Invariably they are optimists. They make provision for growth, but none at all for shrinkage. By their advice, there is now twenty-five million dollars' worth of reserve plant in the various Bell Companies, waiting for the country to grow up to it. Even in the city of New York, one-half of the cable ducts are empty, in expectation of the greater city of eight million population which is scheduled to arrive in 1928. There are perhaps few more impressive evidences of practical optimism and confidence than a new telephone exchange, with two-thirds of its wires waiting for the business of the future.

    最终，这个前瞻性部门将会扩张。如果出现一位天才领袖，它或许会成为第一支真正意义上的实践社会学家队伍，用事实取代目前杂乱无章的理论。它将制定一份涵盖整个美国的“基本规划”，标明每个行业的中心和主要的交通要道。它将基于一个基本事实采取行动：凡是有相互依存的地方，就必然有电话；因此，它将绘制相互依存关系图，展现分散的产业和金融集团，以及将它们编织成国家合作模式的纽带。

    Eventually, this foresight department will expand. It may, if a leader of genius appear, become the first real corps of practical sociologists, which will substitute facts for the present hotch-potch of theories. It will prepare a "fundamental plan" of the whole United States, showing the centre of each industry and the main runways of traffic. It will act upon the basic fact that WHEREVER THERE IS INTERDEPENDENCE, THERE IS BOUND TO BE TELEPHONY; and it will therefore prepare maps of interdependence, showing the widely scattered groups of industry and finance, and the lines that weave them into a pattern of national cooperation.

    迄今为止，没有任何一个国家，甚至包括我们自己的国家，真正认识到长途电话的全部价值。很少有人能想象到它所带来的种种可能性，并意识到即使相隔千里，也能进行真正的面对面交谈。同样令人难以置信的是，身处远方城市的人竟然能像近在咫尺的人一样轻易被找到。这太神奇了，或许要等到新一代人到来，人们才会习以为常并自由地使用它。最终，长途电话无疑将被视为一项极其宝贵的国家资产，因为它能避免因旅行造成的巨大经济浪费。

    As yet, no nation, not even our own, has seen the full value of the long-distance telephone. Few have the imagination to see what has been made possible, and to realize that an actual face- to-face conversation may take place, even though there be a thousand miles between. Neither can it seem credible that a man in a distant city may be located as readily as though he were close at hand. It is too amazing to be true, and possibly a new generation will have to arrive before it will be taken for granted and acted upon freely. Ultimately, there can be no doubt that long-distance telephony will be regarded as a national asset of the highest value, for the reason that it can prevent so much of the enormous economic waste of travel.

    科学所能解释的一切都无法削弱长途通话的奇妙之处，未来或许会出现一位翻译员，将这种奇妙以动态影像的形式呈现在我们眼前。他将使我们能够跟随从波士顿到丹佛的通话，聆听那些飞速掠过的文字。我们将先飞到伍斯特，穿过波基普西的高桥跨越哈德逊河，向西南方向穿过十几个煤矿小镇到达费城郊外，跃过萨斯奎哈纳河，在阿勒格尼山脉蜿蜒起伏地进入匹兹堡的幽暗地带，在惠灵跨越俄亥俄河，掠过哥伦布和印第安纳波利斯，越过特雷霍特的沃巴什河，经由伊兹桥进入圣路易斯，穿过堪萨斯城，跨过密苏里河，沿着堪萨斯州的玉米地一路前行，然后沿着圣菲铁路继续前行，穿越广袤的平原，越过大峡谷的边缘，最终抵达普韦布洛和雄伟的丹佛城。两千五百英里，一千吨铜线！从邦克山到派克峰，只需一秒钟！

    Nothing that science can say will ever decrease the marvel of a long-distance conversation, and there may come in the future an Interpreter who will put it before our eyes in the form of a moving-picture. He will enable us to follow the flying words in a talk from Boston to Denver. We will flash first to Worcester, cross the Hudson on the high bridge at Poughkeepsie, swing southwest through a dozen coal towns to the outskirts of Philadelphia, leap across the Susquehanna, zigzag up and down the Alleghenies into the murk of Pittsburg, cross the Ohio at Wheeling, glance past Columbus and Indianapolis, over the Wabash at Terre Haute, into St. Louis by the Eads bridge, through Kansas City, across the Missouri, along the corn-fields of Kansas, and then on--on--on with the Sante Fe Railway, across vast plains and past the brink of the Grand Canyon, to Pueblo and the lofty city of Denver. Twenty-five hundred miles along a thousand tons of copper wire! From Bunker Hill to Pike's Peak IN A SECOND!

    赫伯特·斯宾塞在他的自传中提到一个令人印象深刻的事实：当眼睛阅读一行文字时，地球已经在太空中移动了三十英里。但在电话通信中，这算是慢速传输了。我们可以用一个简单的日常事实来解释：当你的眼睛阅读这行破折号“--”时，电话铃声已经可以从纽约传到芝加哥了。

    Herbert Spencer, in his autobiography, alludes to the impressive fact that while the eye is reading a single line of type, the earth has travelled thirty miles through space. But this, in telephony, would be slow travelling. It is simple everyday truth to say that while your eye is reading this dash,--, a telephone sound can be carried from New York to Chicago.

    有很多理由相信，对于未来的务实理想主义者而言，最重要的研究对象将是能够创造奇迹的力量。目前，我们国家财富的二十分之一——六十亿美元——正投入到电力开发中。电气时代尚未到来，但它已近在眼前；当一个国家的创造者们集中精力去驾驭这种神秘的力量时，其成果将何等辉煌，无人能够预料。这种力量比人类所能驾驭的任何其他力量都更加强大、更加精妙。

    There are many reasons to believe that for the practical idealists of the future, the supreme study will be the force that makes such miracles possible. Six thousand million dollars--one- twentieth of our national wealth--is at the present time invested in electrical development. The Electrical Age has not yet arrived; but it is at hand; and no one can tell how brilliant the result may be, when the creative minds of a nation are focussed upon the subdual of this mysterious force, which has more power and more delicacy than any other force that man has been able to harness.

    作为一种易于驾驭的能量，电是新生事物。它没有过去，也没有渊源。它比许多现今活着的人还要年轻。在古希腊和古罗马的智者中，鲜有人知晓它的存在，更无人将其用于实际用途。最睿智的人知道，摩擦琥珀会吸引羽毛状物质。但他们将此视为诗意而非科学。腓尼基人中流传着一个美丽的传说：琥珀是少女因单相思而投海自尽的泪水凝固而成，每一颗琥珀珠都弥足珍贵。人们佩戴琥珀作为护身符，象征纯洁。两千年来，无人想到，在这金色的琥珀之中，竟隐藏着一个全新电力文明的秘密。

    As a tame and tractable energy, Electricity is new. It has no past and no pedigree. It is younger than many people who are now alive. Among the wise men of Greece and Rome, few knew its existence, and none put it to any practical use. The wisest knew that a piece of amber, when rubbed, will attract feathery substances. But they regarded this as poetry rather than science. There was a pretty legend among the Phoenicians that the pieces of amber were the petrified tears of maidens who had thrown themselves into the sea because of unrequited love, and each bead of amber was highly prized. It was worn as an amulet and a symbol of purity. Not for two thousand years did any one dream that within its golden heart lay hidden the secret of a new electrical civilization.

    即使在1752年，本杰明·富兰克林在斯库尔基尔河畔放飞他著名的风筝，并捕捉到第一道闪电时，人们对电能也还没有确切的认识。他的避雷针被视为对天神的亵渎，甚至被认为是1755年地震的罪魁祸首。直到摩尔斯电报普及之后，人们才敢于将宙斯的雷霆视为人类的助力。

    Not even in 1752, when Benjamin Franklin flew his famous kite on the banks of the Schuylkill River, and captured the first CANNED LIGHTNING, was there any definite knowledge of electrical energy. His lightning-rod was regarded as an insult to the deity of Heaven. It was blamed for the earthquake of 1755. And not until the telegraph of Morse came into general use, did men dare to think of the thunder-bolt of Jove as a possible servant of the human race.

    因此，当贝尔发明电话时，他以一个全新的想法震惊了世界。他不仅创造了这项发明，也创造了这个想法。儒勒·凡尔纳和H·G·威尔斯都未曾预见过这一点。《一千零一夜》的作者曾设想过飞毯，但他和任何人都未曾设想过飞行通话。在古代文学作品中，除了《圣经》中那句富有表现力的“有声音传来”之外，恐怕找不到一句能用来形容电话的句子。在如今这个更加便利的时代，电话已被视为日常生活中司空见惯的事情；我们很容易忘记，它的奇妙之处有增无减；发明家和科学家仍然能够获得丰厚的荣誉和回报。
